Merchants Steam Navigation Bureau Strike Wave: Mediation Failed Last Night 112

▲All Crew Members Presented Five Conditions

▲Tu Nan, Yu Shun and Other Vessels Joined the Strike

After all crew members of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Bureau launched a strike due to the issue of double pay, Du Yuesheng and others stepped in to mediate. The crew members presented conditions. Yesterday, the Tu Nan and Yu Shun vessels joined the strike. At 8 PM, Du

Page 10

Yuesheng’s residence held a meeting to resolve the matter. The details are as follows:

▲Crew Members' Conditions: All crew members of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Bureau, through a general meeting resolution, yesterday dispatched representatives Jin Yueshi, Xi Wenfang, etc., to the private residence of mediator Du Yuesheng to discuss the following demands: 1. Issue a year-end double pay of one month. 2. Recognize the Seamen's Union. 3. Equal treatment with bureau staff. 4. No arbitrary dismissal of crew members. 5. Year-end double pay is permanent. Mr. Du agreed to be responsible for the first, second, and third of the crew's demands and verbally agreed to the fourth and fifth, but a final decision would be made after discussing with China Merchants Steam Navigation Bureau Commissioner Guo Waifeng at 6 PM.

▲Forming a Union: Among the prerequisites previously resolved by all crew members in a general meeting, the formation of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Bureau Seamen's Union was deemed necessary. To expedite preparations for its establishment, a general meeting was held at 2 PM yesterday at 38 Avenue Edward VII to discuss preparatory matters. It was also resolved that preparations would begin immediately and the union would be established in the shortest possible time to benefit the labor movement.

▲Two Vessels Joined the Strike: Originally, thirteen ships were on strike, remaining anchored at the South Bund wharf and the river channel, awaiting resolution of the double pay issue. Yesterday, the sea-going vessels Tu Nan and Yu Shun also encountered Shanghai after arriving in Shanghai. Their crew members and sailors all reported to the union and unanimously joined the strike. As of yesterday, there were five Changjiang ships and ten offshore vessels on strike. If the issue is not resolved today, the returning Xinjiangtian must also strike. ▲Labor-Capital Meeting: Around 8 PM last night, the crew members received a notification from mediators Du, Li, and Yang, stating that the representative appointed by the capital side, Yu Qiaqing, had already consulted with Guo Waifeng and would soon arrive at Du's residence, inviting representatives of the staff to discuss a peaceful resolution. During the meeting, it was learned that Jin Yueshi, Gong Wenfang, Che Defang, and others were again elected as authorized representatives to go to the mediators' office to discuss the double pay issue. It is reported that there were no significant results, and discussions will continue today. Third Declaration: China Merchants Steam Navigation Bureau Crew Members' Double Pay Petition, Third Declaration: We, the undersigned, petition for fair treatment from the authorities, but our petitions are ignored, and we have no choice but to take action. For the past day or two, we have been grateful to Mr. Li, Du, and Yang for their mediation efforts, allowing the Xinjiangtian to sail, and a resolution seemed near. However, the bureau, showing no sincerity, suddenly fabricated reports to the Municipal Government, attempting to deceive and shift blame. At the same time, they continued to argue strongly against our demands, attempting to unconditionally order the ships to sail. Their intention is to further suppress us, evade responsibility, and confuse the public, deploying a two-pronged approach, which is truly a masterful tactic. We must refute this. Just read the letter from the commissioner to the Municipal Government: first, they accuse us of unauthorized strikes and work stoppages; second, they accuse us of inciting others to join. What kind of language is this? Would a sincere collaborator utter such words lightly? The commissioner recklessly fabricates accusations, only exposing his own vicious methods. It must be understood that we are demanding equal treatment and double pay because the bureau refused to accept it, which led to the petition. When the petition failed to yield results and we faced threats of dismissal and layoffs, we stopped work and waited quietly. Therefore, we are petitioning without success and waiting quietly; we have not gone on strike, let alone incited others. Although the ships are on strike, all work, such as unloading cargo, continues as usual. Can there be such a thing as a strike like this? Our demands for double pay are spontaneous and unanimous; where does this talk of incitement come from? Although the commissioner may believe in his own integrity, he has already pocketed his double pay. However, as soon as we made our demand, he did not hesitate to use all sorts of accusations against us. We deeply regret this for the commissioner. As for the arrears in salary, the commissioner's ability to raise and pay them is, in fact, a kind of effort, and we express our gratitude. But in principle, we believe that it is the commissioner's sole responsibility. If he insists on claiming credit for this, what can we say? As for oppression, the crew members offer a few examples. Kuaili's old mate originally earned 160 yuan, but when he was transferred to the larger ship Jiangjing, his salary was arbitrarily reduced by 20 yuan. Chen Baitao, qualified as a second mate, received a salary of 100 yuan from the bureau. After repeatedly acting as chief mate, he was assigned to Jianghua as a second mate due to disagreements, and his salary was reduced to 80 yuan. Furthermore, He Hailan and Chen Baitao, both resident crew members of the bureau, received double pay in 1919, but in 1920, the authorities arbitrarily revoked it. The bureau's chief engineer, who bears significant responsibility on board, receives a maximum salary of only 180 yuan. Requests for a salary increase are ignored. They also force sea-going vessels to leave port at night, falsely claiming that Bai Mao Shoal can be crossed in the dark, and arbitrarily record demerits. All kinds of oppression are both annoying and ridiculous. Rice subsidies were negotiated by the Navigation Association, not a special favor from the China Merchants Steam Navigation Bureau, and were not implemented by Guo Ren. Why is he taking credit for them? Now he suddenly raises the issue of cheap rice. May we ask if the commissioner intends to advocate for reducing food rations? The situation on land and on water is completely different, as the commissioner is well aware. Why does he use the value of the numbers to deliberately make irrelevant arguments, deceiving the ordinary public? If Western food is brought up, it is completely irrelevant. It must be understood that the cost on board is more than 40 yuan to obtain the same quality of goods worth a little over 10 yuan on land. Moreover, only the captain, chief mate, and chief engineer enjoy this benefit on board. These three are of the same rank as section chiefs in the bureau. How does their salary compare to that of section chiefs? Section chiefs have public funds and can eat and drink as much as they want. Furthermore, rights and obligations are reciprocal. Bureau staff have a fixed working time of six hours per day, while crew members work more than twelve hours at sea, not counting overtime. Even in port, they work more than eight hours. Crew members sacrifice all happiness and opportunities; how can they be compared to bureau staff? This is why the maritime laws of various countries have various preferential provisions for crew members. Now, the commissioner abruptly views this as surprising and wants to overturn global practice. Wouldn't this make knowledgeable people sneer? If he insists on thinking that crew members enjoy excessive benefits, then we are willing to sacrifice the preferential treatment and receive the salaries of bureau staff, but only if we can open the ship at 9 a.m., anchor at 12 p.m., reopen at 2 p.m., and anchor at 5 p.m. for the night, and then go to the dog races and dance halls after 5 p.m. We are willing to remain silent on this. Does the commissioner consider this fair? Can he agree to it? As for paid leave, the ship and the bureau are the same; what are the advantages and disadvantages? Furthermore, crew members each have their own duties. Does the commissioner intend to have colleagues act as substitutes? Isn't this a big joke? It must be understood that there must be section chiefs with special connections in the bureau to rotate like a revolving lantern, but crew members cannot do this in reality, and the law does not allow it (according to Customs regulations, if one crew member is missing, departure is prohibited. May we ask if the commissioner knows this?). Now, the commissioner, as the head of the nation's unique shipping agency, lacks this basic knowledge of the shipping industry. We cannot help but sigh. Moreover, it is not a happy life for one to be sick, and we do not expect to enjoy preferential treatment because of it. If someone considers it happy, then we are also willing to sincerely donate medical expenses. As for the value of the bureau's assets, it is of great importance, and we do not want to investigate the mysteries within. In short, if Commissioner Guo has the sincerity to care for the crew members, he should accept our demands as soon as possible. Why must he constantly compare the benefits of crew members and bureau staff, provoking resentment within the bureau? Otherwise, the work of crew members is risky and arduous, while the work of bureau staff is safe and fixed. The facts are so. Does the commissioner have a conscience? Why must he argue strongly? Is he being too verbose and exerting himself too much? This declaration is intended as a response.

Postal Workers' Union Letter to All Fellow Workers 113

▲According to Chen Si Yi

The Shanghai Postal Workers' Union respectfully addresses this letter to all postal workers. Fellow postal workers, since the invasion of the brutal Japanese and the escalating national crisis, the union has been heartbroken and has organized the Two-Association Anti-Japanese National Salvation Committee to specifically handle Anti-Japanese National Salvation affairs, hoping to fulfill the duties of a citizen. On the one hand, we assess the state of the domestic situation and the hardships of the postal environment; on the other hand, we recognize that the pain of postal workers has not been alleviated. Therefore, we exert our best efforts, intelligence, and strength to maintain good systems in the postal service, stabilize the economic foundation of the postal service, improve the postal service itself, and reform the treatment of postal workers. In the past few months, we have been fortunate to avoid collapse. However, we see that national affairs are deteriorating, internal troubles are multiplying, and the union's affairs are numerous. If we seek to address everything comprehensively, we must rely on the collective wisdom and strength of all fellow workers to urge and encourage each other and work together. It is difficult to achieve success alone. Therefore, we sincerely present several points, hoping that all our fellow workers will encourage each other. At the beginning of the new year, Jinzhou fell, and Tianjin and Peking are in danger. Although the new government has been established, its actions are perfunctory and ambiguous, and everything is new. Our postal workers occupy a central position as citizens, and every action affects the overall situation. In this critical time of survival, we should all cherish the ambition to save the nation and uphold the pure mentality of loving the country. Sharpen our spirits, align our steps, and engage in the training of volunteer soldiers. We should all have the determination to sever economic ties with the enemy. Everyone should contribute their wisdom to make up for the country's salvation, sincerely consult, and seek sound planning, so that the union can draw on everyone's strengths and earnestly engage in the work of Anti-Japanese National Salvation. In this way, we can achieve strength through unity and everyone can fulfill their duties, persist in endurance, and certainly achieve the actual effect of resistance. This is the first meaning of unity to jointly overcome national difficulties. The postal service is the second life of all fellow workers. In recent years, evil internal forces have invaded, such as the separate establishment of the Chu Jing Bureau and the misappropriation of large sums of money to subsidize other parasitic organizations. These are all major tumors that endanger the postal service. Our fellow workers should be deeply aware of the warning of the destruction of both the nest and the eggs, and fear the collapse of the building. We must all unite and resist strongly, so that we can drive away the demons and restore the health of the postal service. We should also persist in endurance, adhere to our duties, and cultivate the postal service itself, so that it will gradually prosper and grow into a bright future. This is the second meaning of removing obstacles to the postal service and promoting postal business. The improvement of postal workers' treatment is limited by the postal economy and cannot be satisfactory. The implementation of postal affairs is limited by the difficulties of the times and is not as expected. For example, the performance evaluation test has not yet been officially cancelled, and the promotion tests suggested by the union have not yet been officially implemented. For example, the boundaries of the branches in this city have been expanded, but the number of mail carriers has not yet been increased. For example, savings insurance and welfare for postal workers have not yet been established. For example, postal routes have not yet been restored. All these are still major issues. There are countless other trivial matters that the union is concerned about and will exert its utmost effort to promote progress. However, the interests of our fellow workers are at stake, and we must exert our sincere efforts and fight together. This is the third meaning of exhausting our efforts to seek thorough liberation. Furthermore, postal workers are the masters of the postal service, and the postal workers' union is a collective of postal workers. Therefore, it is no exaggeration to say that the postal workers' union is the "Ah Dou" of the entire postal service. In recent years, postal workers' unions have sprung up in various parts of the country, achieving remarkable results. However, after the promulgation of the Trade Union Law in 1929, the special regulations for trade union organizations were abruptly cancelled. The trade unions of postal and other special industries suddenly lost their legal basis. Fortunately, our fellow workers have not given up, and their actions and words have all followed the rules. Although there is no law to follow, there is ultimately no excuse to be made, and they can still stand upright in society and move forward in an orderly manner. However, for the sake of prudence, we should request the central government to provide legal provisions as a guideline for action. If it is approved and promulgated, there is no doubt that the future will see results that will surpass today's. Furthermore, how should the organization of postal workers' unions in various places be made sound? How should we support the establishment of postal workers' unions in places where they have not yet been established? How should we promote the realization of the National Postal Workers' Federation? How should we work together to liberate the national postal workers from their suffering? These are all things that the union and all our fellow workers should work together to achieve. This is the fourth meaning of sincere unity and consolidating the foundation of the union. In short, troubles and difficulties are multiplying, and a hundred affairs await to be addressed. It is impossible to achieve success overnight, nor can we expect it in a day. We only hope that our fellow workers, who have been accustomed to and familiar with each other, will be frank and sincere with each other and share our hardships, so that we can jointly achieve the success of enduring hardship. This is what the union fervently hopes for and is happy about. We sincerely inform you, and we hope that you will all encourage each other.

A letter from the National Lawyers' Association requesting to borrow the association's hall for a meeting was resolved to be approved. A letter of reply will be issued for reference. 3. A request from the National Lawyers' Association to convene an interim executive committee and solicit opinions from the legal community on the revision of the Criminal Law and Criminal Procedure Law was resolved to nominate Guo Wei, Zhao Chen, and Shen Junru as three members to attend as representatives. 4. Letters from members Deng Jia Bing and Jiang Chi Ping, reporting that they had resigned from the court for a long time and were not subject to regional restrictions on avoidance, were resolved to send a letter to the Shanghai First Special District Local Court, requesting it to send the names of all personnel who had served as translators or are currently serving as translators in the court, as well as the dates of their appointment or resignation, so that the court's previous letter could be checked and notices could be sent according to whether the restriction period had expired. 5. Committee member Tang Ying Song proposed to pay attention to the urgency of national salvation work. It was resolved to send a telegram to the government, and Committee member Shen Junru was tasked with drafting the text, which would be issued by the standing committee after review. Member Tang Ying Song was also notified to continue attending meetings. 6. Member Ru Bao Yi sent a letter and the appeal documents of the Shanghai Municipal Council, which sued Anti-Japanese National Salvation inspectors for the crime of robbery after being dissatisfied with the court's judgment. It was resolved to refer the case to three members, including Dian Yu Hua, Chen Ze Min, and Shen Junru, for review and report before further review. 7. Member Yang Er Mo proposed that, in addition to posting announcements, the court should prepare an extra copy of judgments, rulings, and instructions to be kept in the lawyers' lounge for easy access. It was resolved to temporarily shelve the proposal. 8. Committee member Shan Yu Hua proposed to submit a request to the Ministry for instructions regarding the time limit for serving judgments, rulings, decisions, and transcripts that should be served in court trials. It was resolved to nominate Committee member Shan Yu Hua to draft the text and submit it to the Ministry. 9. The legal interpretation inquiries submitted successively by members Chen Ying, Xu Guo Wei, and Zhang Fu Kang were resolved to reply by letter that they would not be forwarded until the issue was resolved. 10. Wang Xing Sheng Nan submitted documents alleging that lawyer Yang Chang Chi had engaged in illegal practice and requested review. It was resolved to refer the case to Committee member Huang Han for review and report to the association for handling. 11. He Ji Xiang reported that the Jiangsu Provincial Government's telegram, issued according to the bandit suppression measures, was harsh and severe, and the deprivation of life was excessive. He requested that the association jointly submit a request to abolish it to emphasize the importance of people's lives. It was resolved that all separate laws and regulations that conflict with the Criminal Law would be submitted to the specialized committee for revising the Criminal Law and Criminal Procedure Law for review. 12. Zhong Zhang Yao reported that lawyer Huang Xiu Bo had been commissioned by both parties at the same time. He asked whether it violated the rules of the association and requested review. It was resolved to forward the information to member Huang Xiu Bo for a response. 13. Member Liu Ming Du reported that Judge He Hu Liu of the Shanghai District Court had abused his power and insulted him. He requested that the association review the matter and resolve to submit a request to the Ministry of Justice and Administration for disciplinary action in accordance with the law. Another letter will be sent to the President of the Shanghai District Court, drafted by members Chen Ze Min and Cai Ni Pei, and issued by the association after review. 14. Member Huang Feng Ming reported that member Huang Qi Ni had been arbitrarily detained by the Nantong County Government and requested legal assistance. It was resolved to send a letter to the Nantong County Magistrate, requesting a prompt investigation and release if there was no criminal suspicion, and to pay attention to the lawyer's status and not to detain him arbitrarily. 15. The association's deposits in the China Industrial Bank and the Continental Bank are due. Should they be renewed or changed to other banks? It was resolved to change the deposit in the China Industrial Bank to the Four Banks Savings Society and renew the deposit in the Continental Bank. 16. Applications for membership from lawyers Shi Su E, Wang Bo Xian, Shao Sheng Zu, Yan Guo Qing, Ren Kan, Zhang Shi Ying, Wang Xiao Wen, Chen Zha, Liu Shou Lun, Wu Bai Heng, Tang Hao, and Cai Jue were resolved to be approved and reported to courts at all levels for registration and documentation immediately. The meeting adjourned at 3:00 PM.

Huang Boyu Passed Away in His Shanghai Residence 118

▲Another Senior Statesman in Jiangsu Weakens

Mr. Huang Boyu of Suqian passed away in his Shanghai residence on January 8th. The funeral was held at noon on the 10th, and many mourners attended. Mr. Huang served as the Hunan Provincial Education Commissioner and the Provincial Treasurer, among other positions, and was known for his outstanding political reputation. After the establishment of the Republic of China, he was repeatedly invited to take on important positions but declined, dedicating himself to local affairs. He meticulously planned and greatly benefited the local area in various aspects, including railways, water conservancy, education, and commercial ports. In recent years, he encountered successive major famines. Mr. Huang coordinated with various philanthropists in Shanghai to raise relief funds and work tirelessly despite his illness. His sudden passing has caused widespread grief among the people of Jiangsu.

Wages and Number of Male, Female, Child, and Apprentice Workers. 6. Working Hours. 7. Rest and Holidays. 8. Work Contracts. 9. Subsidies and Pensions. 10. Worker Welfare Matters. 11. Power Source. 12. Leave of Absence. 13. Factory Association Please. 14. Trade Union and Work Rewards and Punishments. 15. Factory Safety Equipment. 16. Factory Sanitation Equipment, etc.

Complaint Regarding Disruption of Customs by Lime Boats 124

More than thirty lime boat owners, including Zhou Xinggen, Wang Rongbao, Jin Zirong, and Sun Rongkun, who transport lime to Shanghai, traditionally have a system where boats are unloaded based on the order of arrival, a custom approved and announced by the authorities. Recently, about thirty lime boats have arrived in Shanghai, waiting for the "Aeolus" to unload lime. However, the newly arrived boat owners, Qian Peirong and Qian Ating, relying on their strength, suddenly jumped ahead to unload lime, openly disrupting the custom. These boat owners believed that such disruption would mean that the lime boats docked in Shanghai would never be unloaded. They reported the matter to the police to stop it, but not only were they disobeyed, but they were also beaten. The police then took Qian Ating's son, Qian Xuelin, into custody, but he was released the next day. These boat owners believe that if this custom is disrupted, their livelihoods will be deprived. Yesterday, they jointly filed a complaint with the Bureau of Social Affairs and the Public Security Bureau, requesting strict punishment to limit disputes.

Murder for Property Case on Yuyuan Road 128

▲ Jewelry Broker Jin Yuancai Stabbed

▲ Perpetrators Sha Guifu and Jin Zhongliang

Jin Yuancai, a jewelry broker from Nanjing, residing at No. 7 Yanhai Road, Nanshi, entrusted Sha Guifu, the younger brother of his in-laws, with diamonds, jadeite jewelry, and other valuables worth over 5,000 yuan to sell a month ago. Sha then resold them to Jin Zhongliang, a fellow dealer. Jin Yuancai, needing to settle accounts, repeatedly asked Sha Guifu for the money, but Sha repeatedly prevaricated, claiming that the items had not been sold. Until about 6:00 PM the night before last, Sha, Jin Zhongliang, and a man named Tang went to Jin's house and invited him out, falsely claiming that the buyer lived on Yuyuan Road and asking him to go to collect the money. Jin believed them and went with them. Unexpectedly, when they reached their destination, Hengchang Lane on Yuyuan Road, Sha and the other two suddenly produced sharp knives and viciously attacked Jin, stabbing him in vital areas. Jin Yuancai was unable to resist, was injured, and fell to the ground unconscious. Fortunately, a Westerner driving by saw the perpetrators, Sha and others, committing the crime in the alley and immediately rushed to report to the patrolling police. The police rushed to the scene, arresting Sha and Jin. Tang, however, took the opportunity to escape. The Westerner took the injured Jin Yuancai to the Red Cross Hospital on Haig Road for treatment. After surgery, he regained consciousness. Yesterday, Jin's condition was still very critical, with over a dozen stab wounds on his neck, back, arms, and other areas. The arrested perpetrators, Sha Guifu and Jin Zhongliang, will be sent to the Special District Court this morning for questioning. The injured Jin Yuancai is 24 years old and has been a jewelry broker for only one year.

Preparing to Establish a Consumer Cooperative for Public Utilities 129

▲ Initiated by the Zhejiang Private Electric Company

▲ The Same Industry Will Independently Order, Transport, and Sell

▲ Resist the Monopoly of Foreign Oil Companies

The Zhejiang Private Electricity Industry Association held a discussion meeting on the afternoon of the day before yesterday at A-11 Jiujiang Road to prepare for the establishment of the China Public Utilities Consumer Cooperative. Wang Gengbo of Changxing Changming Electric Company, Shen Zhiwan of Shengze Fuxin Electric Light Company, Zhang Ziyi of Jiashan Changyao Electric Light Company, Jiang Tiaosheng of Jinhua Electric Company, Zheng Yingqi of Yuanjiahu Huf Electric Light Rice Mill Company, Qian Zuliang of Xiashi Electric Light Company, Zhang Zuyin of Xiaoshan Yongan Electric Company, Shen Sifang of Wuxing Electric Company, Shen Sifang of Tongren Yuziji Electric Company, Wang Cunyong of Taihu Steamboat Company, Wang Cunyong of Tongyuan Steamboat Bureau, Xu Xingbai of Shangchuan Transportation Company, Zhang Youyi of Haiyan Electric Company, Zhang Ziqin of Chaiqiao Zhaoming Electric Company, Ye Chunwu of Shaoxing Daming Electric Company, Tong Zhanghua of Yiwu Electric Company, Zhang Laishou of Pinghu Steamboat Bureau, Han Yimin of Pinghu Minghua Electric Factory, and Sun Zhenyi of Chongde Yongming Electric Company, nineteen representatives in total, elected Han Yimin as the temporary chairman. Shen Siliang first reported on the progress of the project, stating that last fall, Mobil diesel and Asiatica salad oil jointly raised prices to 89.30 yuan, canceling the previously signed contracts with users within a time limit, which greatly affected the business prospects of oil engine users. At that time, Mr. Li Yanshi, in order to avoid manipulation and relieve users' losses, learned that Russian diesel was about to be sold and contacted Russian businessmen several times. However, the diesel had to be imported in quantities of 5,000 tons, which would involve huge costs. It was not appropriate to import rashly a month ago. Mr. Zhang Zuyin of Tianzhong Company mentioned that 500 tons of diesel could be ordered directly from the United States and transported to China, with a reserve capital of 100,000 yuan. Mr. Zhang could also find a way to raise half of the shares from outside and half from oil engine users. This would be easy to do. The colleagues were arranging to proceed, knowing that this would be detrimental to the business of Mobil and Asiatica. Therefore, they agreed in advance not to publicize it in order to facilitate progress. Unexpectedly, the news of this organization's cooperative society was still discovered by the other party, and in order to preempt it, they agreed to lower prices, initially intending to reduce them by 20 yuan, but eventually reducing them by 15 yuan, which was implemented on December 1, 20th year. The motive for the price reduction was this. However, the oil engine users enjoyed the benefit of cheap oil because of the organization of the cooperative. External investments were all aimed at high profits, and at this point, it was difficult to achieve the price, so they no longer intended to join. Therefore, the fundamental way to avoid oil company manipulation is for the same industry to cooperate and operate a purely cooperative society. It is hoped that after the cooperative society is established, oil companies will continue to lower prices. Today, oil machine colleagues from various places have come to Shanghai from afar to gather together. They must have a deep understanding of the meaning of the consumer cooperative. The issue that needs to be discussed now is the problems of fundraising, equipment, oil transportation, etc. Please give your valuable opinions. Next, Zhang Zuyin reported on the cost of diesel ordered directly from the United States, stating that the cost of delivery in the United States was 7.58 US dollars per ton, the freight from the United States to Shanghai was 4.50 US dollars per ton, the insurance premium was 0.026 US dollars per ton, and the domestic import tariff was 1.16 US dollars per ton, totaling 13.26 US dollars per ton, equivalent to 54 yuan in national currency, plus a temporary unloading fee of about 2.5% of the value of the goods, and a regular fee (excluding official interest) of 2.5%, equivalent to 2.70 yuan in national currency. The current market price of Mobil Asiatica Texaco is 74.30 yuan per ton, and the cost of the cooperative is about 62 yuan per ton after deducting all expenses. Therefore, each ton can have a net surplus of 12 yuan at the market price. Calculated at 500 tons, 6,000 yuan can be saved each month, and after 16 months, 100,000 yuan of capital can be raised. After the two reports, the chairman reported that Mr. Zhu Wenjun of Qiaoxie Changda Electric Factory sent two proposals: 1. To raise funds from all oil machine users in the province to establish a machine oil company to order directly from American merchants. 2. To investigate the monopoly situation of Shanghai oil companies to protest and negotiate. These two proposals are insightful, have a global perspective, and are worthy of reference for the cooperative. Mr. Shan Fengxiang of Quxian Electric Company sent a letter stating that oil companies are oppressing users and that measures should be taken to provide relief and be able to stop it, which would greatly benefit the industry. Mr. Cheng Jinhe of Meixi Guangming Electric Company sent a letter advocating gathering capital to organize a large-scale cooperative society to directly sign contracts with the United States to avoid manipulation. All the electrical materials needed for the electrical industry can also be made by the cooperative society itself or purchased and sold to supply our colleagues for purchase and use. In terms of capital, the number of tons of diesel used can be divided equally, or the amount can be limited for allocation. A draft business plan can be drawn up to solicit opinions from colleagues so that they can invest. After the report, the following resolutions were made: 1. The name is set as China Public Utilities Consumer Cooperative. 2. Li Yanshi, Ye Yangwu, Zhang Zuyin, Shen Zhiwan, Zhang Fengshou, Ji Yimin, Qian Zuliang, Zhi Bingyuan, Wang Soubo, Jiang Tiaosheng, Zhang Zhiyi, Shen Sifang, Wang Cunxian, Tao Liumen, Zhang Youyi were appointed as 15 promoters. 3. Li Yanshi, Zhang Zuyin, Ye Yangwu, Shen Sifang, Qian Zuliang, Wang Soubo, Zhi Bingyuan, Han Yimin, Zhang Fengshou, Zhang Minyi, Wang Cunxian were appointed as 11 preparatory members. 4. Ye Yangwu was appointed as the director of the preparatory committee, and Zhang Zuyin and Zhang Fengshou as the deputy directors. 5. The preparatory office was set up at Hanzhong Company, No. 25 Renji Road. 6. The first preparatory meeting will be held at Yizhixiang tomorrow night at 6:00 PM, convened by Ye Yangwu. Yesterday, the meeting was held for the first time at the Yizhixiang Vegetable Society. Zhang Zhiyi, Jiang Tiaosheng, Shen Sifang, Wang Soubo, Zhang Zuyin, Zhang Fengshou, and Ye Yangwu attended. The chairman was Ye Yangwu. The matters resolved were: 1. The capital was set at 100,000 yuan in national currency, and 50,000 yuan was raised, based on the amount of oil used, at 100 yuan per ton. 2. Jiang Tiaosheng, Shen Sifang, Tao Liumen, and Zhang Youyi were added as preparatory members, and all promoters were preparatory members. 3. Yang Bo'an was asked to draft the charter and subscription form. 4. Zhang Zuyin and Zhang Fengshou were asked to establish a budget. 5. The founding meeting will be held in February of the 21st year.

Declaration of the Shanghai Citizens' Federation on Guaranteeing Citizens' Housing Rights 130

Datong News Agency reports that the Shanghai Citizens' Federation, in response to the continuous undermining of the housing rental rights of all residents by major landlords and property owners, established the Citizens' Housing Rights Protection Committee the day before yesterday to safeguard these rights. Yesterday, it issued a declaration stating: Recently, the housing rental rights of our Shanghai citizens have been continuously undermined by landlords and property owners, causing all citizens to face difficulties in both business and residence. This is the biggest obstacle to realizing Dr. Sun Yat-sen's legacy of "equalization of land rights" to benefit residential housing. The legislation of the National Government follows Dr. Sun Yat-sen's legacy, so Article 450, Section 2 of the Civil Code clearly stipulates that "[customs that are beneficial to the lessee shall be followed]." In other words, customs that are not beneficial to the lessee shall not be adopted. How important is the protection of the interests of water renters, that is, "the weak people"? Shanghai landlords and property owners have recently regarded real estate as an object of speculation, ignoring the reality of real estate investment consolidation, and using means such as rent increases and forced evictions to seek profit at the expense of others. A small number of financiers have also fueled the flames, engaging in real estate mortgage transactions, causing the customs that are beneficial to the lessee, such as landlords not being able to ask tenants to move unless (1) tenants are in arrears for more than one month without reason or (2) the houses are dilapidated and must be rebuilt, to be undermined by landlords and property owners and no longer exist. The above facts are clearly contrary to the law, reason, and Dr. Sun Yat-sen's legacy. The association, as a group of citizens, fulfills its responsibility to seek the welfare of citizens, and therefore, it has established the Citizens' Housing Rights Protection Committee to ensure that the habits that should be followed according to law are not shaken and that Dr. Sun Yat-sen's legacy of equalizing land rights to benefit residential housing can be established. We are not afraid of any difficulties. This is our declaration. Shanghai Citizens' Federation.

Investigating the Shape of the Bullet in the Property Dispute Case 131

▲ The Bullet in the Body Is Missing

Zhang Qingxiang of Huayuan Shiqiao, Pudong, colluded with his maternal uncle to kill his elder brother Guoxiang and second brother Yuxiang in an attempt to monopolize the inheritance. However, Guoxiang was injured but not killed, while Yuxiang died on the spot. After the case was accepted by the District Court, Prosecutor Shen Zhaoming, who was in charge of the case, spared no effort to investigate various evidences, and the facts were already clear. However, because the bullet that injured Guoxiang had not yet been removed, Guoxiang was summoned to the case the day before yesterday and went to the orthopedic hospital together to examine the bullet embedded in the neck bone using X-rays. However, inexplicably, after examining the whole body, the bullet was gone. It was thought that it had entered the abdomen. However, when Guoxiang was treated at Baolong Hospital at that time, the hospital took two X-ray photos, one from the side, which was very clear, and one from the front, which only showed the head of the bullet. However, due to the photographic relationship, his face, neck, and bones were completely enlarged, so that the bullet was also larger than its original shape, as if it was fired from a six-inch pistol. The prosecutor is now ordering the forensic doctor to shrink and calculate the shape of the bullet to determine what the original shape was and to consider where the bullet in Guoxiang's body is embedded in order to process the case.

Lawyer Wu Linkun's Father Kidnapped by Bandits in Ganpu 132

Wu Linkun, a famous lawyer in Shanghai, is from Ganpu, Haiyan, Zhejiang. On December 24th of last year, his hometown was attacked by fierce bandits with over 200 people, each carrying guns, knives, and other weapons. Every household was looted, and no residents were spared. The bandits were not satisfied and kidnapped 39 wealthy gentry members before leaving. The next day, 16 people were released, but the whereabouts of the remaining 23 are still unknown. The bandits have not sent letters to the victims to demand ransom. It is reported that Lawyer Wu's elderly father, Mr. Yanqing, was also among those kidnapped. This old man is over 60 years old and is usually very enthusiastic about local public welfare. He especially enjoys helping poor villagers. His family is not wealthy. When the bandits were looting, he was lying in bed, thinking that he was not a wealthy household and would not be noticed, so he did not avoid them. Unexpectedly, he was also kidnapped. After Lawyer Wu heard the news, he tried to rescue him, but he did not know his whereabouts and could not start. Now he is only hoping that his father will send news soon and tell him his residence so that he can proceed with everything.

Extortion Case Involving Chinese Police 133

▲ The Case Cannot Be Established

▲ The Magistrate Reprimanded and Released Them in Court

Sun Zhibing and Shao Tongshun, from Funing, went to No. 33 Linqing Road around 7:00 AM on the 7th of this month to borrow silver dollars from their fellow villager Lu Yongxiang. They quarreled because they were unsuccessful. Lu, seeing that they were about to attack him, fearing that he would suffer a loss, pretended to agree and promised to provide them the next morning. When Sun and Shao went to collect the money, Lu secretly reported to the Yangshupu Police Station, saying that some hooligans were extorting 30 silver dollars from him and pointing out a Chinese policeman, Sheng Lianjia, No. 1969, who was using a pistol to threaten and help with the extortion. The head of the patrol immediately sent Chinese detectives Fei Ruiqing and Liu Changgen to arrest Sun and Shao and bring them to the police station. The head of the patrol asked Lu Yongxiang again whether Chinese policeman No. 1969 was actually present, and Lu claimed that he had mistakenly pointed him out. The detectives also found that the facts were false reports and false accusations of extortion. Lu and Sun Shao were friends for many years. At that time, he only borrowed three silver dollars from them and detained them. The day before yesterday, they were sent to the First Special Court, Court One. The police lawyer Zhang Tianyin stated the previous situation, followed by Chinese policeman No. 1969, who claimed that he saw them arguing and feared that a reactionary incident would occur. He then asked about the dispute over borrowing three silver dollars, so he did not intervene. Unexpectedly, Lu falsely accused him of helping with the extortion at the police station. When questioned, Sun and Shao confessed that they were close friends with Lu Yongxiang. Previously, they requested only three yuan from him, but he refused and secretly reported them to the police station, accusing them of extortion. Lu Yongxiang confessed that he was temporarily confused and afraid of being beaten by them, so he took this action. Regarding the Chinese policeman No. 1969, he did not point out that he helped with the extortion at the police station. Please understand. After Judge Xiao Xiefen verified the confessions, because the case could not be established, he released them all together.

Therefore, when the ship arrived in Shanghai, Lin was sent to the First Branch of the Third District and escorted to the District Court to be investigated and to recover the 1,000 taels fine.

Dahe Steamboat Reports on the Explosion of Firecrackers 136

▲ Passengers Privately Carry Dangerous Goods

▲ The Company Asks for Proper Handling

▲ The Ship Still Sailed Out as Usual Yesterday

Yesterday, Da Da Steamboat Company submitted a report to the Navigation Administration Bureau stating that on January 9th, when the people's Dahe Steamboat was docked at the wharf, preparing to sail out of the port, at 10:10 PM, when passengers were boarding, an unknown passenger privately carried a hemp bag filled with small firecrackers and placed it on the stone head of the rear deck of the second-class cabin. The ship did not know what was stored in it beforehand. Passengers passing by accidentally touched the bag, causing a loud explosion with thick smoke. People on the ship heard the sound and were disturbed, and the order was disrupted. Some people were so anxious that they jumped into the water and were rescued. The crew prepared to provide rescue and tried to comfort them. At the same time, the hemp bag was thrown into the river, and two unthrown firecrackers with explosives were found. At that time, the company was still worried that other passengers might have privately carried the same dangerous explosive materials, so it immediately reported to the Water Patrol Team to send a team on board for a thorough search. As a result, two other passengers were found, one privately carrying four large boxes of matches and the other privately carrying a string of firecrackers, who were detained by the team. Dahe sailed out of the port as usual. The company has no right to inspect and ban passengers from privately carrying dangerous goods. The company has suffered repeated disasters and is extremely painful. In view of the past, it is even more afraid of the future. These types of incidents endanger the lives and property of passengers and are truly impossible to prevent. The bureau in charge of navigation administration must take proper measures to handle the aftermath well without waiting for the company to nag. The Dahe Steamboat Company hereby submits a report on the situation of the firecracker explosion and submits a firecracker with explosives, requesting the bureau to review and approve it.

The Wusong Ship Registration Office of the Shanghai Navigation Administration Bureau has been established. The Public Works Department Sets One-Way Traffic on Jiangxi Road 138

The Public Works Department said that the one-way traffic regulations on Jiangxi Road between Suzhou Road and Beijing Road, going from north to south, have been tried for three months and have been made permanent on the recommendation of the Chief of Police and the Traffic Director. From the perspective of police and traffic conditions, the one-way method has been successful. However, at the beginning of the reform, people protested, which was expected. But once they get used to the one-way traffic, all difficulties will disappear. This method prevents obstruction when loading and unloading goods and materials at warehouses and other places on that section of the road. The one-way traffic method is the same as "no right turn." This may be somewhat inconvenient for those who have business relations in the area, but in narrow roads and intersections, as the number of vehicles and markets increases, for the benefit of the public, it is necessary to make traffic safer and more advanced.

Two Robberies on Hongqiao Town Road 140

▲ Both Victims Injured

Wang Chunquan, a farmer living in Xinqiao, Hongqiao Town, west of Shanghai, was returning home from the town at about 10 o'clock the night before last. Just as he reached his gate and was about to open it, two robbers suddenly appeared behind him, seized him, and robbed him of over forty yuan of membership fees and a cotton robe. Wang resisted slightly, and the robbers struck him on the head with a stick, causing his face to bleed profusely. He fell to the ground, and only dared to call for help after the robbers left. Neighbors heard his cries and came to his aid, helping him back home and bandaging his wounds. Furthermore, Qin Yongchang, a carpenter from Xinqiao, west of Hongqiao Town, was returning home from drinking at a relative's house in Qibao Town at about 8 o'clock the night before last. When he passed by Gujiatang, three people suddenly appeared and grabbed Qin's hands, robbing him of a gold ring and twelve yuan in cash, and stripping off his camel-hair silk robe. When Qin argued with them, the robbers stabbed him in the leg with a knife, and he fell to the ground. He lay there until dawn, when a passerby noticed him and sent him home. It is said that his injuries are very serious and his life is in danger.

Lawyer Does Not Believe He Insulted the Judge 141

▲ It Was Originally the Client's Intention

Lawyer Liu Mingdu acted as agent for Xu Xianglin in a case against his wife, Xu Shenshi, regarding national affairs. A settlement was reached in the conciliation court of the Shanghai District Court, with Xu paying monthly living expenses. Xu Shenshi requested enforcement, and the execution court judge, He Yuliu, issued a summons for arrest. Lawyer Liu filed a protest, and was also dissatisfied during the questioning. As a result, the judge sent Lawyer Liu to the prosecutor's office for investigation. It is now learned that Lawyer Liu was allowed to return home after being investigated by Prosecutor Zhao at 4 PM on that day. He was summoned again the morning before, and Prosecutor Zhao determined that the matter was the client's intention, and again allowed Lawyer Liu to return home, while detaining the client, Xu Xianglin. Lawyer Liu then, last Sunday, attached a letter to the Shanghai Lawyers' Association's Joint Meeting of Executive and Supervisory Committee, requesting a discussion of relief methods, and requesting that the client, Xu Xianglin, be released on bail pending trial.

Special Publication

Jiangsu National Crisis Relief Association's Opinion on Economic Sanctions Against Japan 149

▲ Based on Legal Facts

▲ Ten Methods Proposed

▲ Hoping for National Implementation

This time, Japan is using its violence to invade our Eastern Provinces, and all our people are filled with indignation and heartache, and are urgently seeking to resist. The most effective method is: 1. Armed resistance, 2. Economic sanctions. The former belongs to the power and ability of the government, and our national youth and people have repeatedly petitioned the authorities. The latter belongs to the inherent power and ability of the people. The National Anti-Japanese Salvation Associations have worked hard and struggled for three months. Now, this association is reiterating this to make it clear to all our people that economic sanctions are more effective than armed resistance, that this power is in our hands, and that it is practical. We hope that from now on, we will further strengthen our strength, extend our time, and persevere to the end. The possible points in law and fact are explained separately below: 1) Legal Possibilities. The implementation of economic sanctions by the National Anti-Japanese Salvation Associations can be said to be irreversible. However, if there is no legal basis, it will be difficult to maintain it for a long time. In terms of law, the applicable laws include international law and domestic law. The effect of international law is stronger than that of domestic law. That is, international law has the effect of overriding domestic law. When domestic law conflicts with international law, international law is still effective. The Covenant of the League of Nations is a type of international law, and all member states have an obligation to abide by it. This is the effect of the Covenant. Article 12 states that if a dispute arises between members of the League that is likely to lead to a rupture, the matter shall be submitted to arbitration or examined by the Executive Council. In any event, no war shall be waged until three months after the award of the arbitrators or the report of the Executive Council. Article 13 states that if a dispute arises between members of the League that is considered suitable for arbitration and cannot be satisfactorily resolved through diplomatic channels, the issue shall be submitted entirely to arbitration. Article 16 states that if a member of the League disregards the provisions of Articles 12 and 13 of this Covenant and engages in war, then, according to this fact, it shall be immediately regarded as an act of war against all other members of the League. Other members are responsible for immediately severing all commercial and financial relations with it, prohibiting its people from engaging in various interactions with the people of the Covenant-breaking country, and preventing the people of any other country, whether members of the League or not, from engaging in financial, commercial, or personal interactions with the people of that country. In this situation, the Executive Council shall be responsible for making recommendations to the governments concerned, so that the members of the League can use their land, sea, and air forces to form an army to maintain the implementation of the Covenant. The so-called commercial relations refer to buying, selling, and transportation. Financial relations refer to lending. Personal interactions refer to employment, delegation, contracting, etc. In short, it is economic sanctions. This sanction is not only done by oneself, but also should be done by the people, and can also be done by the people of other countries. But if the violating country engages in war against a member, all other members should immediately assume the obligation of economic sanctions. Then, the people of the country who are harmed by the war can adopt economic sanctions, which is self-evident. This is the legal basis.

2) Factual Possibilities. From the perspective of vendors, those with a little patriotic conscience will definitely not willingly buy Japanese goods. If they mistakenly buy Japanese goods, they will not lose all their value due to prolonged detention and sealing. Moreover, in commercial practice, large quantities of Japanese goods have often been mortgaged in advance. Prolonged sealing will only increase interest. In commerce, losses due to sluggish sales and discounts are also common. Now, in the face of national crisis, suffering this slight loss is not unreasonable. If they deliberately sell Japanese goods for the sake of taking risks and making profits, resulting in losses, they can also be given a small punishment and a big lesson, which is in line with the political principle of sacrificing the interests of a few for the sake of the interests of the majority. This is one possibility. From the perspective of consumers, Japanese goods are luxury goods, and should be prohibited in this time of national crisis and poverty. Japanese goods are necessities, and there is no substitute for domestic goods. There are many substitutes for foreign goods. Moreover, there are four major desires in life, and only food is indispensable. There is no need to rely on Japanese goods. Other deficiencies do not hinder life. This is the second possibility. In terms of methods of resistance, everyone can do it. It is not like armed resistance, which requires special training and special weapons. The patriotic sentiments of our people are surging. If we can get enthusiastic patriots to give advice and guidance at all times using the following methods, even if it is extended from today to one, two, or three years, it will not be as difficult as Gandhi in India. Gandhi was able to advocate non-violent resistance to this extent under the iron heel of the British. Moreover, our country has not been destroyed. Some provinces still have the freedom to resist Japan, and there is the Covenant of the League of Nations as a legal basis. No official loves the country more than I do. It will not be too oppressive. Even now, it is not too late to make amends. 1. All people in the country, regardless of their position, must swear not to buy Japanese goods, not to take Japanese ships, not to interact with Japanese people, not to work for Japanese people, and not to employ Japanese people. 2. All teachers and students in the country's schools, in addition to swearing not to buy Japanese goods themselves, must also do their best to study and publicize and advise the people of families and various social groups not to buy Japanese goods, and to contact various sectors to organize patriotic national salvation groups to investigate Japanese goods and effectively resist them. 3. All employees of various stores in the country, regardless of what kind of goods they sell, must swear not to buy or sell Japanese goods. If there are a few unscrupulous merchants who secretly import Japanese goods and sell them privately, they must report the facts to the patriotic national salvation groups and severely punish them as a warning to others. 4. All railway workers, ship workers, dock workers, truck workers, and all other transportation workers in the country, in addition to not buying Japanese goods, must swear to stop transporting Japanese goods. 5. Women across the country, when choosing daily necessities for their families, must swear not to buy Japanese goods, and must pay extra attention when shopping, and not buy Japanese goods that impersonate domestic goods or Western goods. 6. The financial sector across the country, regardless of banks, money houses, or silver firms, must swear to sever all ties with Japanese people, and sever all ties with unscrupulous merchants who secretly import Japanese goods and sell them privately. 7. All goods sold by exporters across the country to foreigners must state that they must not be resold to Japanese people. If it is found that the goods have been resold to Japanese people, they must be warned and efforts must be made to stop it. 8. Importers across the country, when ordering goods from foreign merchants, must state that they must not impersonate them with Japanese goods, and must not ship them on Japanese ships. If the above situation is found, efforts should be made to resist it. 9. Members of the Tianjin Lawyers' Association across the country must share the responsibility of defending lawsuits related to economic sanctions against Japan, and must not defend or handle negotiations for unscrupulous merchants who have been sanctioned by the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association, in accordance with the resolution of the Shanghai Lawyers' Association. 10. Administrative officials and judges in the country must base their decisions on the patriotic conscience of the people and implement the protection of patriotic people from being deceived by unscrupulous merchants who buy and sell Japanese goods, in accordance with the spirit of Article 16 of the Covenant of the League of Nations. The economic relationship between Japan and our country is very close. The previous eight boycotts of Japanese goods were laughed at by Japan for their five-minute heat. This time, Japan dared to risk the disapproval of the world and occupy our Northeast with force, also because our people's resistance to Japanese goods only has a five-minute heat and is not enough to be feared. If our people can be firm and persistent, then Japan's economy will inevitably develop five flaws. This is the only way to sanction Japan. May our people work together.

Reader's Communications

Four Major Political Reforms 150

Break. Down. Party. Bias. Gather. Talent.

Open. Up. Public. Administration. Implement. People's. Constitution.

Implement. Conscription. End. Recruitment.

Promote. Universal. Education. Encourage. Learning.

Zhang Ke Gong

The foreign crisis is urgent. The Eastern Provinces have fallen, and the whole country is shocked. Internally, warlords are playing with soldiers, bad governance is emerging daily, and the Communist Party is rampant with bandits everywhere. The floods in 18 provinces last year were rare in Chinese and foreign history. People are not living, and the country is on the verge of ruin. Talented people concerned about the times have risen up to save themselves, knowing that to resist foreign aggression, we must first pacify the country; to pacify the country, we must first eliminate factions and engage in political reform together. However, with sores all over, where to start? Grasping the key lies in being appropriate. Now, based on what I have seen and heard, I will briefly offer my foolish opinions: 1. Break down party boundaries and gather talent. The party occupies an absolutely small minority of the entire population, and not all talented people belong to the party. Observing under the past party rule, there is a lack of talent within the party, and opportunism and competition are rampant, and politics is deteriorating daily, which easily leads to the autocracy of those in power, which leads to the disintegration of the party. Outside the party, even if there are people of superior intelligence and talent, they are unable to serve because of the constraints of the situation. Thus, the party gradually becomes a special class to the people, and the people gradually develop fear, jealousy, and hatred towards the party, and gradually generate the heart to suppress and abandon it. At its extreme, it will inevitably evolve into a special class struggle of the entire nation, or some may criticize it as a feudal system of intrigue, which, although an overstatement, is not without reason. 2. Open up public administration and implement the people's constitution. Once party boundaries are broken down, a people's constitution should be implemented. In this transitional era, the minimum requirement is that the members of the legislative and supervisory chambers must be thoroughly elected. All measures to raise public debt, try new taxes, and increase the burden on the people must be approved by the legislature, and their use, as well as all income and expenditure of the state finances, should be strictly reviewed by the supervisory chamber. The Examination Yuan is responsible for selecting talents, which is of great importance to the future of the country. It should be organized by the national academic community, and the government should select the best candidates for appointment. The above three chambers are all regularly convened institutions and do not need to be established on a permanent basis to save expenses and facilitate execution. The lower-level party departments in various places should be resolutely abolished in the shortest possible time and replaced by people's autonomous organizations. 3. Implement conscription and end recruitment.

Conscription is a necessary element of democratic politics. There can be no master who has no strength to control his servants. This is the reason for all the internal wars since the Republic of China, the violation of popular will, and the military dictatorship. At this time of the rampant Japanese and the poisoning of the Communist bandits, it is even more urgent. All active soldiers should be transferred to the border to recover lost territory. When the people's military strength is gradually established, they should be gradually demobilized and returned to the fields. Those who have contributed to defending against foreign aggression and have outstanding military achievements should be given appropriate arrangements. The current major problems of the country and the suffering of the people are the intrusion of Japanese slaves, the harassment of the Red Party, and the frequent cyclical internal wars. These three cannot be eradicated without implementing conscription. 4. Promote universal education and encourage learning. Promoting universal compulsory education is also a necessary condition for democratic politics. Otherwise, only the rich can enter school, and the majority of the poor will remain ignorant like deer and pigs, and will not know what national politics is. Those who are now in charge of the country only know how to implement tutelage and do not plan to promote universal compulsory education. I am afraid that their tutelage will have no end. As for researching academic matters and writing books, they should be vigorously encouraged, and there should be no restrictions that hinder the progress of evolution. Even if there are one or two who do not comply with the law, in my opinion, if there is no factual manifestation, they should only be corrected, and not immediately convicted. The above is just a rough outline. At first glance, it seems distant and difficult to achieve immediate results. However, to recover the scattered hearts of the people, eliminate the hidden dangers everywhere, correct the source, and gradually achieve governance, there is no other shortcut to be found. In addition, promoting morality to rectify the people's will and revitalizing industries to enrich the people's livelihood are also urgent tasks that cannot be delayed. Real industries owned by the people should be thoroughly protected. Due to limited space, I will not list them separately. (Ding) (Shift Reward for Assistance)

Miscellaneous Notes on Sino-Japanese Military Strength 153

— Shi Yan Ye

There is a Mr. Sun in Jinshan. Formerly a professor at Feng Yong University, he later studied military affairs at the Japanese Military Academy. Recently, due to the national crisis, he returned to China. I heard him talk about the state of Sino-Japanese military strength, which is summarized as follows. Japanese men, upon reaching the age of twenty-two, are immediately enlisted in the military and undergo military training for a period of two years. After discharge, they become reservists. In the event of a national emergency, they are required to be mobilized for service upon the order of the military. However, this obligation only lasts until the age of forty-one, after which they are no longer obligated to participate in combat. Currently, the number of active Japanese military personnel, combined with these reservists aged twenty-four to forty, totals no more than three million. This constitutes their main force, a modest number not to be feared.

Japan is extremely well-stocked with military equipment. The bullets used for target practice by cadets at the military academy are all marked with the year "Taisho [Emperor] such-and-such." I have not seen any marked with "Showa [Emperor]". The bullets seized from the Japanese bandits who recently caused trouble in Tianjin were also manufactured in the fifth year of the Taisho Era. Their abundant stockpiles are thus evident. Although their country has seen little war and does not require such reserves, the fact that they maintain them reveals their ambition.

We Chinese people flee at the mere rumor of the Japanese army, as if the Japanese army were as fearsome as tigers. In reality, their skills are quite ordinary. Their physical strength is not as great as rumored, and their intelligence is not superior to ours, and may even be inferior. Those who go to study at the military academy must first undergo six months of practical training in the Japanese army. In terms of physical comparison, they are similar to us. In terms of teaching, the Japanese have not yet understood it, while we are already familiar with it. During the May 3rd Jinan Incident, according to a certain commander of ours in Jinan, the Japanese army was actually a paper tiger. Their tactics were so poor that it was evident upon contact. We merely tremble at their reputation and change color at the mention of war.

There are three supreme military and political organizations in Japan: the Ministry of the Army, the General Staff Headquarters, and the Naval General Staff. The Ministry of the Army is responsible for administrative matters.

Ma Yongzhen and Yellow Tooth Beard 154

— Yan Zi

Chinese boxing has traditionally been divided into the Shaolin and Wudang schools. Shaolin emphasizes strength, while Wudang emphasizes flexibility. Most martial arts performers in the Jianghu [martial arts community] start with Shaolin. Ma Yongzhen, who lived forty years ago, was a master of Shaolin. I was fortunate enough to see him as a child. Ma performed in Shanghai on North Shimen Road (i.e., North Fujian Road), with a large yellow banner that loudly proclaimed: "Feet Stomp the Yellow River, Sweep Across the Four Seas; Fists Strike Both Northern and Southern Capitals," to demonstrate his invincibility. Yellow Tooth Beard, a French police detective, was also a master of Western boxing. He brought an interpreter to Ma, wishing to test his skills. Ma smiled and refused. Yellow Beard suspected that Ma was afraid and insisted on a match. Ma explained the difference between Chinese and Western boxing, stating that if he made a mistake, it could cause trouble for which he would not be responsible. The interpreter relayed this to Yellow Beard, who stubbornly refused to accept. Ma said, "Let's just try it. How about we step on roof tiles and hook our index fingers to test our strength?" Yellow Beard agreed. They proceeded to compare strength in this manner. As soon as they hooked fingers, all the tiles under Yellow Beard's feet shattered. His face turned red, and sweat poured down his forehead. The onlookers knew that Ma was deliberately yielding, while Yellow Beard was in an embarrassing situation. At the time, there was a gatekeeper named Jia at the Shilu Tianxian Theater. He was from Shandong, seven feet tall, with fists as big as buckets. He was an experienced martial artist with great strength. Hearing of Ma's arrogance, he wanted to embarrass him. He waited by Ma's side for several days. One day, he caught a glimpse of Ma practicing punches with his disciples. He took a string of one hundred cash coins from his pocket and threw it at Ma from a distance. Ma sensed a wind behind his head and dodged it. It hit a disciple behind his ear, causing a slight cut. Ma calmly said, "A true hero never resorts to sneak attacks. If there is a strong man, why doesn't he come forward for a contest?" He ordered his disciple to buy Western paper and held a corner of the paper, standing ten steps away. Ma announced to the crowd, "My hard kung fu has reached its peak. I can defeat him with internal strength. Watch my small skill." He then pointed a finger at the paper from a distance. The paper suddenly pierced through. The spectators applauded, and tossed money rained down. Jia, witnessing this, knew he was no match and quietly retreated. I was only twelve years old at the time, but I still remember the scene vividly. The General Staff Headquarters is in charge of military command, etc. The dispatch of troops must be ordered by the Naval General Staff. The General Staff Headquarters and the Naval General Staff are both directly under the Emperor and not subject to the control of the Cabinet.

According to a certain military expert, the total number of soldiers in our country is actually more than 2.2 million. As for guns, there are not enough to equip them, as not every soldier gets a gun. There are no stored-up bullets, they are all consumed in internal wars. On average, each soldier is given at most two hundred bullets. If a general attack is launched, they will be used up in a single day, and everyone will sigh at the emptiness. If we declare war on Japan, we should be able to cope with their active military personnel. However, Japan has reservists aged twenty-four to forty, so we must also urgently train militia as a backup. A shortage of bullets is not to be feared, but by leading them ashore for hand-to-hand fighting, we can surely destroy them. According to what I have heard, there is something Mr. Sun does not know. In the northern countryside of our country, nineteen out of ten families have guns and corresponding bullets. I heard that in Haizhou alone, there are 50,000 guns. Considering all of the North, there should be no fewer than several million guns. The method they use to store guns is to pour candle wax into the gaps of the gun and apply oil to the outside, making it like a wax gun. Buried underground, it will not rust or decay for many years. In the event of an emergency, they can be taken out, and the oil removed. Therefore, I say that today's militia should be quickly gathered in the North. They have guns, bullets, and training. A strong army can be assembled in an instant.

Anecdotes of Xu Jingwo 155

— Qing Qu

Xu Jingwo was a bookseller who lived in Shanghai and set up a book stall under the Shengping Tea House on Fuzhou Road. At that time, Zhang Taiyan from Yuhang and Zou Weidan from Sichuan advocated anti-Qing sentiment, and revolution was at its height. However, sellers were often targeted by detectives and did not dare to display such books. Xu alone gathered them all without leaving any out, and he was content. Therefore, every day after the lamps were lit, a crowd stood around him. Those who were fascinated by these kinds of books all competed to buy them, and his business was uniquely prosperous.

Xu spoke with a Ningbo accent and wore Western clothes, but he was quite witty and always made people laugh. His background was actually unknown. He had two daughters. At that time, it was fashionable in the female world to wear short jackets and long skirts with only sleeves, but he had them cut their hair short, letting it fall loosely over their shoulders, just like the fashionable women of today. He was the first to start the trend. My deceased friend Wang Zhiheng and I often liked to talk with him. One day, a Japanese man came, who was also familiar with him. Xu pointed at him and said, "[Those who worry about the present only know to guard against Russia. Comparing them to the tigers and wolves of the Qin Dynasty, they do not know that in twenty years they will have to guard against these rats even more]." Those who heard this secretly laughed, and the Japanese man also looked ashamed. To this day, I remember it and admire Xu's foresight, lamenting that I cannot reach it.

Later, he was reported by those who were jealous. Jiang Governor Duan Fang urgently wanted to arrest him. Shanghai detective Mi Zhanyuan took Xu to the provincial capital for interrogation, which almost cost him his life. Someone who knew the situation said that Xu was nicknamed "Wild Chicken King" and was a rogue. What revolution would he be involved in? Therefore, he was released. It turned out that Shanghai's small newspapers, such as "Youxi Caifeng" and "Tongwen", were competing to open flower lists, and Xu, to avoid arrest, had also been a teacher of a courtesan. Who would have thought that this leisurely activity in the realm of pleasure was also a way to protect himself wisely? After Zou Weidan died of illness, no one dared to bury him. Liu San from Minhang used three acres of his good land for the burial, and Xu managed the matter. His noble righteousness was like this. Today, few can speak of it, so I have recounted it.
