There is an ancient saying about a beard hanging down like hair, but looking at Ari, one can only laugh at Lu Yun's limited knowledge.

The hair of Polish peasant woman Berri Jia, Boli Ni Jia, is thirteen

A Word from Old Man Ma Xiangbo, Ninety-Three Years Old 157

In the Republic of China, in Beijing, there was a publication called "Wansong Yeren Yan Shanlu." The opening chapter said, "In recent years, people's hearts have been treacherous, and customs have been corrupted to an extreme. All those mature gentlemen and upright people cannot help but be saddened by what they see and want to come up with all sorts of ways to maintain order. Although the methods are different, they are all a kind of painful effort to save the world. However, the most common opinion among them is that a country cannot be established without religion. When asked why it cannot be established, they say that religion has a kind of power to restrain people's hearts and unite groups. When asked how it has this power, they say it is because religion has superstition. But superstition is unacceptable. For example, popular morality books that advise people to do good actually have stories about saving ants resulting in passing the imperial examination as Number One Scholar, and burying snakes resulting in the honor of being a prime minister. Think about it carefully, the value of a Number One Scholar is just a few ants exchanged, and the honor of a prime minister is obtained just because of a snake. Furthermore, Qin Hui and Yan Song were both Number One Scholars and prime ministers. What good deeds did they do to accumulate that karma? Therefore, Zhao Yun Song has a poem that says, 'Scholars of the world like to criticize Buddhism, wanting to exhaust its essence. I only speak of its rudiments, which are clearly and easily understood. Its teachings strictly prohibit killing, so life can flourish. But it cuts off the desires of men and women, not allowing humans to be born. This will cause the universe to be filled with animals and devoid of people. Is this the principle of creation? Its poison surpasses the pit of Qin. Try to use a long tongue to argue, what will you say?' Some say that if there is no reincarnation and karma, would it not discourage gentlemen from doing good and encourage villains to do evil? Furthermore, in ancient times, the lifespan of Yan Hui was short, while the lifespan of the bandit Zhi was long. The principle of delivering blessings and punishments is inevitably overturned. How can this comfort people's hearts and calm their anger?' I say that these principles are not difficult to explain. For example, ancient people praised King Wen's great virtue, even saying things like 'Shining in Heaven, at God's side.' If Jie and Zhou were extremely evil, could they be placed in the same rank as King Wen? Surely not. If not, then they must be in the opposite position. At the end of the Ming Dynasty and the beginning of the Qing Dynasty, there was a Wei Shuzi who was also a famous figure in the Confucian world. He wrote four essays on the topic of Hell, although they were not entirely clear, they still had some meaning. His main point was that in the world, rewards and punishments are chaotic, and good and evil are mixed. People who are extremely evil and heavily sinful, or who die of old age, like the traitors Cao Cao and Qin Hui, and the lewd tyrants Yang Guang and Wanyan Liang, the state's punishment only goes as far as dismemberment. Those who are extremely cruel do not fear death. What should be done about them? Furthermore, they often do not suffer worldly punishment. Therefore, there must be a Hell to make them wish for death but not be able to obtain it, tossing and turning among knives, saws, and cauldrons for millions of years without end. Bribes and pleas are useless. Filial sons and kind grandsons cannot substitute. Evil retribution falls upon their own bodies and does not affect others. Alas, this is the ultimate! Furthermore, he said, 'I firmly believe that Hell is necessary as a matter of principle, while reciting scriptures and worshiping Buddha to eliminate disasters and expiate sins is impossible as a matter of principle. If worshiping Buddha could eliminate sins, then powerful families could be as evil as they pleased, but only need to spend one-tenth of their wealth to avoid punishment. Then Buddha would be an evil rascal and crafty gentry who indulged in sentiment and pleas. Buddha should be sitting in the chief seat in Hell!' Therefore, the two words 'superstition' cannot save the world. Guo Jun Futing is also an upright person who wants to maintain the world and people's hearts. He plans to re-engrave the Yin Zhi Wen with illustrations to awaken the world. The good thing about his book is that it has illustrations. Even those who cannot read can see it and warn themselves." Therefore, the old man happily quoted the words of Yeren to refuse his request.

Feet six inches. When she was fifty-two years old, she won first prize at an exhibition in Treistein.

▲ The Italian Prime Minister forbids the capture of swallows. Every year, tens of thousands of swallows migrate from England to Africa. This time, when they flew through Italy, Vienna was experiencing heavy snow and severe cold. Tens of thousands of these swallows froze to death. When the people of Vienna saw this, they felt pity and loaded three motorized airplanes from Venice to rush to their rescue. It is said that thousands of people went to the rescue. All the swallows scattered in the gaps of the eaves of the Vienna houses were captured and placed in buckets and fed insects. In this way, the airplanes transported up to 40,000 swallows to Venice every day. If the weather does not clear up, they may be transported to Naples. Therefore, Italian Prime Minister Mussolini, upon hearing the news, immediately ordered a ban on capture. However, Italy has a great fondness for swallows and is secretly capturing and raising them.

A Record of Rongma Shuanglou (6) 158

— Seeking Happiness, Master of Qizhai

Chapter One: An Unrivaled Courtesan Lives in Solitude, Cherishing Her Beautiful Family; A Student in a Foreign Land Wanders, Forging a Strange Romance. At first, I thought that anyone, regardless of gender, could strive to improve and seek advancement. Given the vastness of the world and the abundance of opportunities, there was no need to worry about not finding a path to develop and manage. However, when I seriously tried to get started, I was dazzled and confused by the myriad possibilities. I couldn't find a suitable place to start. If I were to lightly believe what people said and act rashly, it would seem inappropriate. I couldn't make up my mind and hesitated for some days, and I still hadn't accomplished anything. Gradually, I began to focus on finding a lover. In today's world, it is more legitimate for men to come forward and do things. I would find an honest and useful young man, and we would combine forces. I would strategize and help him embark on the path to success. This would be similar to doing it myself. Moreover, as a lonely, unmarried woman, I had tasted the flavor of loneliness and felt confused in my heart. I felt that everything was too monotonous and that life was somewhat meaningless. To treat this empty and anxious heart disease, I needed to borrow the honey-like love between men and women to irrigate and nourish it. It was a great need, and I was eager to find a lover who met my conditions and hoped they would arrive soon. Unfortunately, the conditions I had set were too demanding. Where could I find such a person in a short time? I couldn't treat my aspirations as a game and slightly lower my standards to accommodate vulgar people. Walking alone without a place to turn, my heart was filled with strange boredom. Gradually, I thought of temporarily resuming a more romantic lifestyle to dispel my current bad mood. However, I could no longer go to brothels. I would treat the few wealthy patrons I knew from my days as a courtesan, as well as some famous figures of the present, as friends and socialize with them. I could put on a performance on occasion, which would be harmless. These people had long admired my beauty and had mourned my entry into a wealthy household and my separation from the streets. Now that I had fallen into the dust again and was a free agent, who wouldn't want to chase after me and take advantage of me? Naturally, I could go anywhere and receive a grand welcome. Before long, the general society was stirred up by my activities. Everyone unanimously praised me as the most popular social flower. Every day, I was invited to banquets and parties. I was invited to someone's home to play cards and eat, or I was invited by a certain minister to dine at a restaurant. Or I was invited by a certain general to listen to a play in a theater box, or I was invited by a certain celebrity to watch a movie or go to a dance hall. Both Chinese and foreigners were welcome, and both old and new were welcome. In terms of entertainment, everyone was trying their best to please me. I would no longer feel lonely. In addition, there were many gifts and rewards, such as gambling money, which supplemented my income. Although these people were ambitious and treated me like a private prostitute, secretly harboring ulterior motives and wanting to lure me back into the brothel, I was already much more experienced and skillful. I was able to adapt to the situation and keep them at arm's length, playing them around and leaving them frustrated. And I remained free as the sky.

Founding Assembly of the Secondary School Education Association 160

The Shanghai Secondary School Teachers' Union held its founding assembly yesterday at 1:00 PM in the auditorium of the Qingxin Middle School. More than 180 members attended. The association's charter was approved, directors were elected, a declaration was issued, and several important cases were resolved. Details are as follows:

Opening Ceremony: ㈠ Addition of a presiding chairman ㈡ The entire audience stood at attention to salute the Party Flag and the National Flag and the portrait of the Prime Minister. ㈢ Reading of the Prime Minister's will ㈣ The chairman reports the purpose of the meeting ㈤ The representative of the preparatory committee reports the preparations ㈥ Discussion of the charter ㈦ Election ㈧ Review of the declaration ㈨ Temporary proposals ㈩ Adjournment. First, the presidium was elected: Zhou Yingcai, Lin Muguan, Yang Deshou, Song Bingqin, Huang Yan, Su Wenguang, Liang Zhongyuan, and seven others were elected as the presidium, and Lin Daoyuan and Li Youbai were the recorders. After the ceremony, Chairman Zhou Yingcai reported on the purpose of the meeting. Then, the representative of the preparatory committee, Yang Deshou, reported on the preparations. ▲ Revision of the Charter. The revised charter of the Secondary School Education Association is as follows: ㈠ Name: This association is named the Shanghai Secondary School Teachers' Union. ㈡ Purpose: The purpose of this association is to connect emotionally, study academics, promote culture, cultivate national strength, and improve life. ㈢ Membership: Any teacher in a secondary school in Shanghai, who is introduced by two or more members of this association and approved by the board of directors, may become a member of this association. ㈣ Organization: (A) This association has a board of directors to handle all affairs of the association. The board of directors consists of 21 members elected by the general membership meeting. The standing directors are seven members elected by the directors. The chairman is elected by the standing directors. The term of office is one year, and they may be re-elected. (B) This association has a secretariat to assist the board of directors in handling the affairs of this association with various schools. The number of secretaries is unlimited. One person from each school is hired by the board of directors. ㈤ Membership fee: Each member pays half a dollar every six months. Special donations are decided by the board of directors to be raised temporarily. ㈥ Meeting schedule: (A) The general membership meeting is held at least twice every semester. If necessary, it may be convened temporarily with the approval of the board of directors and the proposal of 20 or more members. (B) The board of directors meets once every two weeks. (C) The secretariat meeting is convened by the board of directors at any time. ㈦ Address: The address of this association is temporarily borrowed from this city (the board of directors will notify you after borrowing). ㈧ Supplementary provisions: Matters not covered in this charter shall be amended by the general membership meeting.

▲ Election of directors. The results of the election are as follows: Chen Jicheng, Pan Yangyao, Tang Tianxiong, Wu Jiangleng, Wang Dunchang, Li Youbai, Wu Ziqian, Lin Muguan, Xu Renwu, Zhou Yingcai, Xu Derun, Lin Daoyuan, Huang Rencheng, Song Bingqin, Song Liangqi, Wang Chengliu, Jiang Wenbao, Huang Yan, Zhang Youlin, Yang Deshou, Zhang Xinlong, Fu Guobin, Zhang Weixin, Chen Wen, Shen Wenhua, Lu Songan, Zhang Jiashou, Liang Zhongyuan, and twenty-eight others.

▲ Adoption of Proposals. The following proposals were adopted in the temporary discussions: ㈠ To urge the government to recover the lost territories in the Northeast, to be handled by the board of directors. ㈡ To formulate a plan to guide young people, to be discussed in detail by the board of directors. ㈢ To telegraph Wang Jingwei, Chiang Kai-shek, and Hu Hanmin to immediately go to the capital to jointly face the national crisis, or to hand over political power to the people, to be drafted by the members of the board of directors. ㈣ From now on, every January 10th will be a holiday to commemorate the establishment of this association. ㈤ The board of directors shall find ways to recruit members. ㈥ To publish a publication. ㈦ The board of directors should establish a service referral office as soon as possible.

▲ Declaration of Establishment. The wheels of the era are advancing rapidly. Looking at the trajectory of history, from scattered to gathered, and surveying the societies of various countries, all kinds of occupational groups have strict organizations. Our country's industrial and commercial industries each have corresponding organizations. We, who have the responsibility of guiding secondary education, do not dare to consider ourselves the pioneers of the times, nor do we dare to consider ourselves the laggards of the times. At a time when internal strife is frequent and foreign troubles are pressing, the times and the environment do not allow us to be like Lao Tzu's chickens and dogs, who hear each other's voices but do not interact with each other until they die. Since we have recognized our environment and understood the mission we bear, we have organized this association in accordance with the general principles of social evolution and the spirit of mutual assistance and cooperation. The work that should be done is divided into the following: 1. This association is not a dummy organization, but a labor organization. It brings together people who are engaged in the same profession, regardless of their differences, to gather the essence of their thoughts and meet the needs of the times, so as to seek the long-term welfare of secondary education. 2. Secondary education takes on the deficiencies of primary education and opens up the path for researching specialized academic subjects. Its responsibilities are very important. In this era of scientific prosperity and academic innovation, how can our country's culture be promoted and how can world culture be introduced and discussed? These are the important tasks of this association. 3. The waste of thought and the chaos of scholarship are worse than ever before. Young students have weak wills and novel opinions. They rely solely on personal intuition to act arbitrarily. This kind of emotion, if used well, can benefit the country and the people. Otherwise, if high pressure is applied, the future will be unimaginable. As for how to guide young people out of confusion and how to lead students back to the right track, the members of this association should [plan ahead] and learn from each other's strengths to provide appropriate guidance. This responsibility is also what we should bear. 4. Modern education is superficial and impractical, and cannot be trusted by people in society. In the future, we should learn from the past and be more careful. We should provide students with practical and effective education, and demand reasonable living standards for ourselves. In other words, how should the school curriculum be compiled? How should books and instruments be equipped? How should teaching materials be compiled? How should theories be studied? Everything, everything, must be [mutually observing and good] [choosing good and following it] to reach the ideal path. 5. Recently, the Japanese pirates have become increasingly deep. The comrades of this association have always been patriotic. In this time of national crisis, we should, on the one hand, urge the government to recover the lost territories, and on the other hand, guide young people to cultivate national strength in an effective way, laying the foundation for saving the country through academics. The above five points are just the major points. Other things, such as thrift and savings, promoting research, and organizing cooperative agencies, are all things that we should strive for.

Shanghai University Presidents' Luncheon Meeting 161

▲ Presidents of both public and private universities attended

▲ The Educational Association used the occasion to express its views

The Shanghai University Presidents' Luncheon Meeting, the tenth of its kind, was held yesterday (Saturday) on the eighth floor of the Hua An Building. The hosts were Hu Shuhua of Tongji University, Xiao Youmei of the Music Academy, and Zhang Shouyong of Guanghua University. Guests included university presidents Chu Minyi, Zheng Hongnian, Li Zhaoning, Sheng Zhenwei, Ou Yuanhuai, Liu Zhanen, Cao Huiqun, Jin Tongyin, and Wang Jingqi (representing Ding), totaling over twenty people. After several rounds of drinks and dishes, Hu Shuhua first delivered a speech on behalf of the hosts, expressing hope for a prosperous new year for all the presidents and raising a toast to their health. He then introduced Kang Xuanyi, representative of the preparatory committee of the University Faculty and Staff Association, explaining the association's spirit, which is as follows: ㈠ The association is purely motivated by a selfless spirit, striving to become a purely free and moral union, without any background influence. ㈡ The organizers have no intention of monopolizing; the organization is also quite democratic. In principle, all school staff are considered faculty and can enjoy equal rights, with no bias towards presidents or professors. All universities, large and small, have an equal opportunity to participate. ㈢ The source of funds is a contribution of fifty yuan from each of the initiating universities, collected by Zhang Shouyong and Zheng Hongnian and stored at the Shanghai Bank. Withdrawals require the signatures of both Zhang and Zheng. No donations have been solicited from any other sources. ㈣ Membership fees are not currently being collected; only those who complete the membership procedures have an obligation to pay fees. ㈤ The association is not in a hurry to have all Shanghai faculty and staff join; it is currently being started by a small group of people, with the intention that the entire academic community will benefit from it in the future. University representatives do not have to represent the entire school; members can join the association voluntarily from each school. ㈥ The association will never adopt an antagonistic attitude towards any other organization, as various organizations can coexist and achieve the same goals through different paths. Mutual suspicion would only show the world a lack of magnanimity. ㈦ The association is pragmatic and aims to be substantial and sound, avoiding empty rhetoric and unrealistic goals. Finally, it hopes that all schools will understand any past shortcomings in the association's work and sincerely invites all schools to join in cooperation, especially hoping to concentrate all Shanghai educational talent, unify the organization, show no signs of division, and preserve a pure and untainted reputation. The postponement of the association's representative assembly is also a compromise and does not involve waiting for non-member schools to produce representatives. The association is willing to accept the strictest supervision from the entire Shanghai academic community and will sever ties with the academic community and submit to public criticism if it ever tarnishes the reputation of the academic community. Zhang Shouyong and Zheng Hongnian then spoke in succession to supplement the explanation. After hearing this, many university presidents expressed their willingness to elect representatives to join in cooperation. The meeting concluded at 4 PM at the YMCA in the Eight Immortals Bridge area, where the date of the representative assembly will be decided.

Heroes Trapped in Frigid Winds of Malaya Succumb to the Iron Hooves of Donghua 163

▲ A 2-2 Draw in the First Half

▲ Result: 2-4 Defeat

Today's Match Against Jinan

The Malayan Chinese Overseas Football Team, visiting Shanghai for the second time, played its first match yesterday afternoon at 3 PM at the Chinese Baseball Field. Everyone exerted themselves, eliciting continuous cheers from the audience. However, due to their unfamiliarity with fighting in the frigid climate, the heroes were greatly troubled in the last forty-five minutes. The first match thus ended in defeat. Donghua, on the other hand, displayed an organized lineup and courageous spirit to extinguish the strong enemy, and their reward of a 4-2 victory was well-deserved. Referee: He Chunhui.

Donghua Team Lineup:

Zhou Xianyan, Li Ning, Guan Xunan, Chen Pu, Tu Kaiyuan, Chen Jiaqiu (Upper), Jin Yuanqian (Lower), Qian Jingyong, Chen Hongguang, Dai Linjing, Chen Jiaqiu (Lower), Li Yichen (Upper), Chen Yutian.

12,000 People Support Football 164

The Malayan skills have long been admired by football fans at sea, and the Donghua talents are also outstanding figures of the time. Once the decision to meet was made, Jin Shenfu Road suddenly saw a rush of traffic, and the baseball field became a sea of people. The scale of the excitement was no less than the rematch between Donghua and Norsonburg. There were 8,827 six-corner seat tickets and 1,325 one-yuan seat tickets, totaling 10,152 tickets (with an estimated income of 5,738 yuan). The actual number of people was around 12,000. The cheers and shouts of these 12,000 people encouraged the soldiers' courage and fueled the interest in the football match, which can be said to have indirectly made them the protagonists of the day's event.

Malaya Unaccustomed to Cold 165

Malaya grows under the tropics, unlike Donghua, which is accustomed to the cold. Once in the harsh, cold wind, they feel their muscles shrink. At first, they can resist, but after a long time, four or five people suffered leg cramps due to the cold, and their equal or superior position was reduced to a state of coercion, ultimately leading to a 2-4 surrender. It was not their fault; it was the severe cold climate that caused it. Regarding the team's overall skills, running and heading are their strengths. As for individual skills, goalkeeper Huang Jinbo is agile and has made countless saves. Inside forwards Guan Xinde and Xie Jinfu have sharp feet and will advance whenever there is an opportunity. Center forward Li Wenjie is good at charging, but his progress was limited due to Tu Kaiyuan's surveillance. Jian Dehui's midfield is very promising, and the substitution of Huang Kehou in the second half created gaps in the center, giving Donghua opportunities to move. Both inside backs Xu Jintang and Yu Zhuohua have heads as hard as iron, often defending unyielding in the face of overwhelming attacks. Left winger Liu Jinrong is more impressive than the two right wingers Deng and Xia, with Deng's skills being above Xia's. Both forwards are average. Looking at the overall situation, they were awe-inspiring and free in the first half, but retreated to a corner and lacked defense in the second half.

Origin of Donghua's Victory 166

Donghua's victory was due in part to the enemy's unfamiliarity with the climate, but the team's excellent performance was also universally acknowledged. Tu Kaiyuan's midfield is becoming increasingly masterful and has become the best Chinese midfielder in recent times. Chen Pu is experienced, Chen Jiaqiu is clever, and Jin Yuanqian, a talented forward, has more strength than intelligence. However, Donghua's third and fourth goals were both said to have been created by him, making him a lucky general. Li Ning and Guan Xunan advance and retreat in an orderly manner, as solid as a copper wall and iron barrier. Goalkeeper Zhou Xianyan was slightly alarmed, but there were no major flaws, and his merits and demerits canceled each other out. Dai Linjing did not show much in the first half under the close pursuit of the enemy Jian Dehui, but he was free to move after being replaced by someone else in the second half. His once horse-riding-and-arrow-shooting goal was truly amazing. Li Yichen has strong feet but lacks speed. Chen Hongguang's charge is outstanding and his courage is exceptional. Chen Yutian is promising and still agile. Qian Jingyong has not made much progress and often commits offside. The turning point for Donghua was the substitution of Chen Jiaqiu for Li Yichen, making the five forwards incredibly fast.

Malaya Surprised at the Start 167

As the silver whistle blew, the Malayan army attacked, and Guan Xunan headed the ball out twice, removing the danger. Donghua took the opportunity to counterattack, and goalkeeper Huang Jinbo was the first to bear the brunt, resisting the strong enemy. Center forward Dai received a supply from Yutian and shot at the goal, but Huang caught it with a casual hand. Then, Qian Jing kicked a corner, and Huang jumped out from the inside again at the appropriate point. Li Yichen charged, and Chen Hongguang shot with the momentum, but Huang saved it safely again. Huang's amazing performance was praised throughout the stadium.

Donghua Safe After Hitting the Goalpost 168

From then on, Malaya's momentum was strong, and the ball was brought in from the left. Guan Xinde picked it off to the center, and center forward Li flew forward. Goalkeeper Zhou, seeing the situation was not good, rushed out to save it. At this time, Malaya's siege had been formed. After fifteen minutes of attacking from the left and right and advancing from the front and back, right winger Deng picked it off, Guan Xinde dribbled past a person, and goalkeeper Zhou missed. The ball suddenly cut onto the goalpost, and the goal was spared. This failure to score was a foreshadowing of victory. Right winger Chen took the opportunity to invade, and goalkeeper Huang pushed it out. Hongguang advanced again, and Huang dealt with it properly. Malaya came again, Guan Xinde shot, and goalkeeper Zhou caught it and dropped it again. Center forward Li rushed to pounce, and goalkeeper Zhou lay on the ground to block it, finally announcing safety.

Changes Within Five Minutes 169

At the twenty-third minute, Chen Hongguang, in the enemy's formation, passed the ball to Li. Li Yichen dribbled the ball forward and suddenly shot it straight to the goal. Goalkeeper Huang was too slow to block it, and Malaya lost the goal. Looking back, the five Malayan tigers arrived in succession. Xie Jinfu shot from the ground, and goalkeeper Zhou wanted to save it but was too late. Within five minutes, each side scored a goal, which can be described as a great change.

A 2-2 Draw in the First Half 170

After this change, Donghua's military morale was stimulated. The forwards passed each other and attacked. Center forward Dai used clever tactics, but goalkeeper Huang rushed out and broke it, and his skill could be seen. Li Yichen continued to attack, but was also blocked by the goalkeeper. Xie Jinfu of Malaya shot again, hitting the goalpost and rebounding out of danger. Dai avoided the attention of others and picked it off from the right. Chen Yutian hit the goalkeeper's body and struggled several times. Suddenly, midfielder Tu flew his leg and hit the goalpost with a bang, entering the net. Donghua took a 2-1 lead. The situation changed again, and Malaya took the offensive. Guan and Li defended strictly. After a few minutes, right winger Deng passed to the center, and Guan Zhude shot smoothly, hitting the target and creating a 2-2 draw in the first half.

Photo of Malaya and Donghua Together (Taken by Huiguang)

▲ Donghua Takes the Advantage in the Second Half

As the second half started, Malaya's performance was reduced due to the influence of the climate. At the same time, Donghua's forwards were more agile than before, and they were mostly on the attack within forty-five minutes. If it weren't for the sound inside backs and reliable goalkeeper, the overall situation would have been unimaginable. At the tenth minute, Donghua suffered a scare, but Zhou threw it out. Afterwards, Chen Jiaqiu and Chen Hongguang successively attacked fiercely, but they failed every time they encountered goalkeeper Huang. At the twenty-fourth minute, Chen Hongguang finally scored a goal. Before long, Chen Hongguang bent down and greeted the ball with his head, but goalkeeper Huang caught it again. Finally, center forward Dai shot in a horse-riding-and-arrow-shooting posture, scoring a goal. As a result, they won 4-2.

Financial: Gold Market Spirited Last Week 174

▲ Four Consecutive Weeks of Increases... Breaking Through 700 Taels

▲ Limited Transaction Volume, Most Long Positions Tightened: The gold market was particularly spirited last week, but the situation was peaceful and without special fluctuations. Due to the New Year's holiday, trading only opened on Tuesday. It was slightly sluggish at first, probably due to the influence of the continuous rise in the silver market, which caused the opening price to be 678.5 taels. Later, due to the tightening of the foreign exchange market, it soared, breaking through the 700-tael mark. However, the daily range was only within 10 taels. On Thursday, it suddenly reached a peak of 711 taels. Finally, the silver price rose, and it retreated back below 700 taels in a soft environment. The total weekly fluctuation was 32.5 taels, with a net increase of 7.9 taels, marking four consecutive weeks of increases. The British and American silver markets and foreign exchange, etc., all tended to shrink. This was a reverse reaction after the consecutive small declines in British and American exchange rates. As a result, the trading price of the US exchange rate was leveled out, and the initial quoted price was around 40 taels, later 50 taels. Initially, Yufeng and Yongguang took in red bars, so it was increased to 15-16 taels, then suppressed to around 10 taels. However, the trading volume of the exchange was not large, only 20,000-odd lots, and most of them were held by large long positions, refusing to let go. It is said that Yufeng, Yongheng, Fuchang, and a certain bank all held long positions, while the Dalian gang held short positions, along with Yifeng, Yuanmao Yong, and Tongtaichang. The general situation of the week's progress is recorded below.

Three Consecutive Days of Increase After Opening, Slight Decline at the Weekend: From the beginning of the week, January 4, the large bar increased by 1.25, and the American silver also increased by 1.25. However, all banks and gold exchanges were on holiday, so there was no trading activity. On Tuesday, the large bar increased by another .0625, while the American silver shrank by .125. The advance order increased by .25, and the US dollar only increased by .125, due to the small exchange rate. Internally, the British market was flat and the American market was tight. The bidding for gold had already started. The initial opening price was 678.5 taels, a decrease of 7 taels compared to the previous New Year's Eve. It then rose by more than 10 taels, reaching 96 taels, because the buying was extremely smooth. In the midday market, a certain Wu sold, causing it to fall to 89 taels, and then 90.5 taels in the afternoon. The afternoon opened at 90.8 taels, then 2.8 taels, and closed at 90.02 taels, with a total increase of 4.7 taels. The difference between the front and rear markets was 17.5 taels, but there was little turnaround. The red bars were increased to 15-16 taels. On Wednesday, the large bar continued to rise by .0625, the silver market did not change, the advance order remained the same, and the US dollar decreased by .125, which was to offset the exchange rate. The internal market still saw the British market rising and the American market falling. The gold gangs first grabbed and then released. The initial opening price for gold was 93.5 taels, an increase of 3.3 taels, then 2.3 taels, and then it broke through 700 taels, reaching 700.05 taels, due to the pursuit of large players. Later, because of news from abroad that cash could be used to pay war debts instead of gold, the market became depressed and selling became rampant, plunging more than 9 taels, suddenly to 91.2 taels. The midday closing price was 94.6 taels. The afternoon opened at 97 taels and closed at 94.1 taels, another increase of 3.9 taels. On Thursday, the large bar had already shrunk by .25, the silver market shrunk by .625, the advance order shrunk by one level, and the US dollar shrunk by half a yuan. The internal market was also tight, and the grabbing was unremitting. The initial opening price for gold increased by 9.4 taels, to 703.5 taels. Then there was a slight range, but the buying was agile, reaching 711 taels. Suddenly, large players came to sell, immediately falling to 05.5 taels, then 10 taels, causing panic. The midday closing price was 07.7 taels. The afternoon was 05.5 taels, then it fell from 06 taels to 03 taels. By the closing price, it was 09.5 taels (a total increase of 29.5 taels in four consecutive days), an increase of 15.4 taels compared to the previous day. The daily range was 8 taels. Wu and Yifeng both sold. On Friday, the large bar shrunk by .375, the silver market increased by 0.125, which was a rebound in the exchange rate. The advance order shrunk by one and a half levels, the US dollar did not change. The internal market also had a different trend, with the British market tight and the American market loose. The initial opening price for gold was 700 taels, immediately falling by 9.5 taels, especially with Chengfeng Yong selling first. However, all firms bought, and it immediately rose by 4 taels, to 04.5 taels. Later, with more selling downstream, and hearing that the American people opposed the American government not following the convention to stop Japan's violation of China, the market declined, plunging by 8-9 taels, the midday closing price was 95.6 taels. The afternoon was 96.5 taels, then 8.5 taels. Later, due to more selling and the turbulent situation, it fell to 95.1 taels. Suddenly, Wu and others competed to buy, and it returned to 701.5 taels. By the closing price, it was 99.8 taels, a slight decrease of 9.7 taels compared to the previous day, which was a reaction to four consecutive days of increases. The daily range was 9.4 taels. On Saturday, the large bar increased by 0.125, the silver price increased by 0.375, the advance order did not change, and the US dollar only increased by 0.125. The internal market tended to loosen. The gold market opened small by 5.8 taels, to 94 taels, then from 6.2 taels, it returned to 3.2 taels. Yiji continued to offset the shorts, reaching 96.6 taels. Afterwards, there was a slight fluctuation, forcing the midday closing price to 92.4 taels, a decrease of 6.4 taels compared to the previous day. The range in the second half of the day was only 3.4 taels. The market was flat. The high and low prices of the British and American silver markets and the gold bidding are listed below:

Securities Market During the First Week of the Year 177

▲ Sharp Decline of Three to Four Yuan… February Futures Trading Commenced on Saturday

The situation of the Shanghai securities and bond market during the past week (from January 4th to 9th): The Exchange had originally scheduled to open on Tuesday, but due to other reasons on that day, there were no transactions in either spot or futures. Therefore, there were only four trading days in the past week. Many types of spot goods were traded daily, and activity was not sluggish. The total turnover for the week was 155,800 yuan, including 26,000 yuan each for 1921 Customs Bonds, 24,000 yuan for Consolidated Tax Bonds, 23,500 yuan for 1920 Bonds, 18,300 yuan for Sixth Year Bonds, 18,000 yuan for Salt Tax Bonds, 6,000 yuan for 1921 Bonds, 5,000 yuan for Customs Bonds, and 4,000 yuan each for 1921 Relief Bonds and Disbandment Bonds, and 1,000 yuan for Seventh Year Bonds. However, there was no trading in 1996 Bonds. The futures market remained sluggish, with major players taking a wait-and-see attitude and market activity as quiet as before. On Wednesday, Thursday, and Friday, only January futures were traded, with February futures opening only towards the weekend. Daily trading volume, for example, was only over 2.6 million yuan on Friday, and only 4 to 5 million yuan on other days, totaling 16.445 million yuan in four days. This included 2.665 million yuan for January Salt Tax Bonds, only 5,000 yuan for February Salt Tax Bonds, 2.625 million yuan for January Consolidated Tax Bonds, 10,000 yuan for January First Month Bonds, 2.4 million yuan for January 1920 Bonds, 5,000 yuan for February First Month Bonds, 2.175 million yuan for January 1921 Bonds, 10,000 yuan for February First Month Bonds, 2.075 million yuan for January 1921 Relief Bonds, 10,000 yuan for February First Month Bonds, 1.64 million yuan for January 1920 Bonds, 30,000 yuan for February Bonds, 1.12 million yuan for January Disbandment Bonds, 10,000 yuan for February First Month Bonds, 1.005 million yuan for January Consolidation Bonds, 5,000 yuan for February First Month Bonds, 260,000 yuan for January Customs Bonds, 5,000 yuan for February First Month Bonds, only 340,000 yuan for January Sixth Year Bonds, and only 45,000 yuan for 1996 Bonds. As for the price fluctuations of various bonds during the past week, the market was very weak on Wednesday, with all parties tending to sell and demand being scarce. The supply and demand for bonds were very disparate. At the beginning of the morning, the prices fell sharply. Consolidated Tax futures then fell to the limit price and trading was suspended. Other bonds such as 1920 Customs Bonds, Bonds, Salt Tax Bonds, etc., also almost reached the point of suspension, with prices falling by about two or three yuan. This was due to the large-scale Japanese advance in recent days, the fall of Jinzhou, and the imminent danger of Jehol Province. There was great shock in Tianjin and Beijing, and foreign media were anxious. Empty words of calm and non-resistance led to the loss of territory on a daily basis, causing panic among the people and a significant impact on the securities market. In the following two days, the situation did not improve, and all parties were in a state of stagnation. The bonds were then in a state of fluctuation, with no major changes. There was a slight rise on Thursday, and a general fatigue on Friday, with only minor ups and downs. However, on the last day of the weekend, there were new changes in the situation. Although our domestic politics were chaotic, the United States suddenly issued a strong note of declaration to Japan. Although it is still difficult to predict how the great powers will react to this, we are both happy and worried. The market sentiment was again anxious, and selling surged, causing prices to fall by about two or three yuan again. Furthermore, other factors that affect the bond market, although the external situation is the biggest reason, the free retention of tax revenues by foreign provinces also deals a major blow to the bond market. Therefore, the current situation in the bond market cannot be reversed by empty words of maintenance. It is necessary to take a holistic approach and consolidate credit before recovery is possible. Silk and Tea: Double Cocoon Silk Goods Are Scarce and Prices Are High 182

▲ Cocoon Merchants Hoarding Goods... There is Almost No Formal Market for Remote Song Goods. In the past year, the spring, summer, and autumn silkworm cocoon harvests in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces have all been poor, and the production of double cocoon silk has also decreased accordingly. The European sales of double cocoon silk are still relatively strong. Among the six double cocoon silk factories in Shanghai, more than half are operating at times. The sales of double cocoon cocoons are quite strong, resulting in increasingly thin inventories. Currently, the number of double cocoon cocoons in Shanghai warehouses is limited, and cocoon merchants are hoarding goods. Opening prices are still high, with ordinary goods requiring seventy or eighty taels. High-quality goods from remote areas are even scarcer, with almost no formal market.

However, the trading of British thin galvanized iron was very prosperous yesterday, with a total of more than 10,000 sheets traded. Although the market price did not improve immediately, it felt much better than before. It is estimated that a 36-foot sheet is worth one tael and three qian, and a 37-foot sheet is worth one tael and two qian. However, futures transactions were slightly cheaper by one or two cents.

Small Forum 185

Shanghai Gains Another "Patient" Fortunately... 186

If someone were to investigate and count the number of "important figures" and "secondary figures" currently staying in Shanghai for [medical treatment], there would be at least a dozen or more. The nation is facing so many difficulties, and the important figures are so frequently ill. This is truly a case of [misfortunes never come singly].

Mr. Feng Yuxiang has always been in good health. This time, in order to [jointly overcome the difficulties of the times], he resolutely came south. When Mr. Feng arrived in Shanghai, all the newspapers, large and small, said that Mr. Feng's [complexion was full, and his spirit was abundant]. However, as soon as he arrived in Shanghai, he also quickly became ill. On the 7th, he telegraphed the Chairman of the National Government, Lin Sen, saying: [Yuxiang is recuperating in Shanghai and has not yet fully recovered and is currently under treatment]. Ah, Mr. Feng is sick again. Shanghai has gained another "sick" "important figure." Did Mr. Feng really get sick? Some say: [I ate with Mr. Feng somewhere the day before yesterday, and I saw that his appetite was better than others, his voice was loud and clear, and his spirit was high, with no signs of illness]; some say: [At 4:15 p.m. the day before yesterday, Mr. Feng went to the Nar Hospital on Avenue Joffre to visit Mr. Wang Jingwei, and they talked for half an hour;] and others say: [On the 7th, Mr. Feng wrote a letter to his old comrades, earnestly urging them to be physically strong]. If Mr. Feng's illness is a fact, then the above news is certainly not a fact. Conversely, if the news is a fact, then Mr. Feng's illness is at least a doubtful fact.

If Mr. Feng was originally not sick but insisted on saying that he was sick, then that is [feigning illness] or [pretending illness]. Feigning illness and pretending illness are the traditional bad habits of Chinese officials. We do not hope that Mr. Feng has also contracted this bad habit. [If we agree, we stay; if we disagree, we leave]. There is no room for evasion or pretense. Every politician should have this kind of open and aboveboard attitude. Feigning illness and pretending illness are just sneaky activities. What we, the common people, need are officials who are:

Healthy,

Honest,

Open and aboveboard,

Serving the people and the country.

We must eliminate all [sick officials] and all [corrupt officials]!

Popular Literature 187

Silk Xiaofeng残月 188

[Willow banks, dawn wind, waning moon] and I get it from…

1. The window of the West Building! At that time, my dormitory in the school was a large room facing west. There were more than ten people in the same dormitory, and my bed was exactly laid by the window. Often in the middle of the night I would wake up naturally, and naturally no longer sleep. I would sit up, breathing the cool air that was like wind but not wind, staring at the half-circle of the bright moon, and the battlements on the city wall hundreds of steps away, both of us silently facing each other;

2. On Guandi Temple Square! Later, because I liked quietness, one winter, I moved to a deserted Guandi Temple three miles away from the school. Every day, before the east was even white, I would rush to school to eat breakfast at 6:30. I stepped on the snow-like heavy frost all the way, and thought of [moonlight in front of the bed]. When I looked up, sure enough, there was a bay of waning moon and a few scattered stars in the dim sky, constantly flickering against the cold north wind;

3. On the top of Mogan Mountain! One summer, I stayed on Mogan Mountain for two weeks. On the day I went down the mountain, according to the prevailing custom at that time, I rushed to a friend's place to get on the sedan chair before dawn. As I walked through the winding stone steps, my head was constantly sprinkled with falling bright pearls and white jade, and my feet trampled on the white plum blossoms and magnolia petals that were spread all over. I was really surprised and happy. Oh, it turned out that the bamboo all over the mountain, the dense layers of thin branches and leaves, were listening to the good intentions of the clear wind in the dawn, and were filtering down half of the clear brilliance of Chang'e;

4. Inside the pavilion! Now I can only run around in Shanghai for food and clothing. Thanks to the kindness of the landlord, the direction of the house is adapted to the local conditions. In the low pavilion, my dormitory, based on the position of the North Star at night, actually faces northwest. Therefore, although I can never see the round moon or blow the cool wind of summer or the warm wind of spring, I can often see half of the white jade plate, which is assumed to be obscured, and I can enjoy some of the summer heat and winter cold morning air in the window, and I am satisfied;

Where will I get it in the future? I do not know.

Rebirth Zhang Feng 189

A fiery red-haired steed,

Carrying a familiar hero,

Isn't it a casual record of reading history, remembering,

Perhaps a contemporary celebrity,

Straining his waist and shoulders, twisting his strength,

He wants to wield his sword to resist the bandits and drive them away,

But it's just a fake statue,

Making people sigh and sigh in vain,

Sighing and sighing, recalling two or three times,

Suddenly, his beard and eyebrows rise,

The enemy under the ground hates that we have never met,

Delaying an unfinished old history,

Specially come again to caress this good landscape,

See how many generations of jumping beams are tolerated in this world,

Looking up at the long sky, a long drink of bitter wine,

In the wind and snow, the fiery liver and gallbladder,

Popular Science

New Theory That Eating Sweets Does Not Harm Teeth Chang Tian 190

[Eating too many sweets will definitely cause tooth decay] was originally an old saying, tamed into a powerful hygiene motto in society. Even the general class of doctors all believe this to be a matter of course and often advise people with children not to eat too many sweets. However, according to scientists, sweet foods are rich in nourishment. It is extremely beneficial for children to eat them. It is indispensable during the developmental period. So, is there a considerable relationship between dental disease and sweets? It is necessary to solve it immediately.

In recent years, there has been a female doctor in England named Mrs. Mellanby, who has done specialized research on this issue. She is a specialist in orthopedics and dentistry, so her research is of course very credible. According to the results of her recent research, it is believed that there is no direct relationship between sweets and dental disease. Children who eat sweets, under certain circumstances, can not only not develop dental disease, but also because sweets are rich in nourishment, it is not too much to eat them.

Mrs. Mellanby's statement is certainly not empty talk. She has actual experiments. Initially, she used puppies to test them. She fed dogs with sugar food every day. After they grew up, not only did they not see dental problems, but their body bones were better than normal dogs. At the same time, she also raised several puppies, feeding them candy on the one hand, and removing various fats and vegetables from their daily food on the other. After a long time, those dogs actually developed dental problems. Therefore, she determined that the onset of dental disease is definitely not due to the scourge of sugar food, but because the food lacks certain ingredients. This ingredient was subsequently determined to be [Vitamin A.]

[Vitamin A] is very rich in fat, especially in animal liver: green vegetables and radishes turn into this ingredient once they enter the human abdomen. Therefore, those with dental diseases, if they eat more of these things, can heal themselves without treatment. And if children can eat more cheap and good-quality green vegetables and radishes, then even if they chew candy all day long, they will not chew out dental problems.

Since Mrs. Mellanby published this opinion, it has attracted the attention of the medical community in various countries around the world. Many doctors in England have also used their own children as actual experiments. On the one hand, they carefully used a large amount of Vitamin A to supply the children, and on the other hand, they let them chew candy at will. According to their reports, the experimental results were satisfactory, and none of the children suffered from dental disease. I am introducing this new discovery to the people of the country, and I also hope that domestic doctors will rise up and test it.

Street Sociology

Shanghai's Air and Sunlight Almonds 191

A's friend rented a rear living room from a chauffeur's second landlord. On the partition wall between the rear and front living rooms, there hung a painting of [Zhong Kui Catching Ghosts]. In this way, it completely blocked all the sunlight in the rear living room, making it pitch black. After my friend A moved in, he negotiated with the second landlord, asking him to move the painting away, allowing a little sunlight in. The reply obtained from the negotiation was... [Move it away, but you have to add a dollar], and finally, after adding a dollar, my friend bought a ray of sunlight from the second landlord's hand.

Soon after, I and a friend rented a garret in an alley near the French Park. Experience told us... the rent demanded by the second landlord was particularly expensive compared to the general rent. We asked him what the reason was. His reply was... [This house is near the park, and the air is very circulated, [so the rent is more expensive].

The words of the two second landlords vividly portray a commodified Shanghai. Shanghai is a Shanghai for the rich. Everything in Shanghai is commodified. The rich occupy everything, and the poor do not even have the possibility of freely receiving the air and sunlight that nature bestows on all things.

Shanghai is a paradise for the rich and a hell for the poor. East, West, South, North.

Feng Yuxiang's Poems Ze Pu 192

The other day, the supplement contained K's [Feng Yuxiang's Wonderful Couplet]. I was reminded of a good poem by Feng Yuxiang. Mr. Feng Yuxiang is a famous [soldier] in China. During his trip south, he was warmly welcomed by young students and mass organizations. You have surely seen the attire of this old gentleman, either at a welcome meeting or in the newspapers. Doesn't he look like a farmer? It is said that when he set off from Taiyuan, he bought two large bags of sesame cakes, and he had not finished eating them when he arrived in Shanghai!

Now I want to introduce Feng Yuxiang's wonderful poem, artist Xu Shiqi painted a picture of a rickshaw puller, and the old gentleman wrote such a seven-character ancient poem:

One person sits in the car, one person pulls,

Both are human beings, yet like cattle and horses,

Heavy oppression is truly painful!

Only hope that a benevolent person will come to save him.

Toothpicks are a Luxury K 193

After returning from participating in the International Statistical Conference, Liu Dajun, on January 3, talked about his impressions of passing through Soviet Russia at a welcome banquet held by the Economic Society: He said that one day, the Sino-Russian Conference delegation held a banquet in a very luxurious hotel in Moscow to treat him. After the meal, when he asked the waiter for a toothpick, the waiter brought a box of matches. Mr. Liu thought that the waiter had misunderstood his meaning, so he made a gesture with his hand and asked a person who was good at Russian to explain it to him. The waiter replied apologetically...

[Toothpicks are a luxury. We do not manufacture them in our country, and foreign goods are prohibited from being imported.]

Although this is a small matter, it is conceivable that on the one hand, the Soviet Union has been working hard to increase production in recent years, and on the other hand, it has also been working hard to reduce waste. Everyone lives the life of a worker and enjoys simplicity, so from the government's important officials, everyone can be clean and impartial, which is indeed a big reason.

Shanghai Stories

Shanghai Stories (5) 194

▲ Chen Huacheng Died in Battle

At that time, Niu Jian, Governor-General of Liangjiang, was stationed in Shanghai, and Chen Huacheng, Jiangnan Admiral, was stationed in Wusong. Niu Jian arrived at Wusong from Shanghai and, seeing the towering British warships, towering more than ten feet above the sea embankment, with smoke covering the sky and dense guns and cannons, was very frightened. Huacheng tried his best to comfort him, saying: [The foreigners only rely on guns and cannons. I have experienced the ocean for fifty years, and I have been born and died in artillery fire many times. Today's fire attack is quite promising. I am willing to take the lead. If I can thwart their edge, and the reinforcements advance in one go, the British are really not enough to be defeated]. At dawn on the 8th, Huacheng first ordered the artillery to open fire and sink two British warships. When the British army landed from the East Fort, the guards Wei Yinfu and others guarded the West Fort and died in battle. Huacheng saw that the army had no reinforcements, beat his chest and stamped his feet, and sighed deeply, saying... [The English barbarians have been rampant for many years. Today, they have been slightly thwarted, and the overall situation in the interior is of great importance. Unexpectedly, the success of the project will be defeated in one fell swoop. The commander (referring to Niu Jian) will kill me].

All the soldiers fled, but Huacheng still fired the artillery alone and fought hard. Later, because he was attacked from the front and back, he was shot and died spitting blood. Huacheng was from Fujian. At that time, he was already a 76-year-old man. His great fearless spirit is worthy of posterity's worship! It is also said that his body was buried in the City God Temple.

Chapter 2: Establishment of Concessions 195

▲ The Treaty of Nanking

After British warships left Shanghai and bombarded Zhenjiang, causing extremely brutal destruction and killings, they went on to disturb Yangzhou and attack Nanjing. The Qing court then appointed Qiying, Ilibu, and Niujian as plenipotentiary ministers. On July 24th, Daoguang 22nd year, they concluded the Sino-British Treaty of Amity, also known as the Treaty of Nanking, with British envoy Pottinger.

Within the Treaty of Nanking, there was a clause stating: [The Great Emperor graciously permits British people to bring back their families and reside in the five coastal ports of Guangzhou, Fuzhou, Xiamen, Ningbo, and Shanghai, to trade and conduct commerce without hindrance]. From this point on, Shanghai's doors were flung open, and a new destiny began. However, upon examining the original text of this treaty, it did not grant foreigners the right to lease land in China, nor did it designate any areas for residence (i.e., concessions).

Following the establishment of the Treaty of Nanking, both the United States and France sent ambassadors to the Qing court to request permission to trade in the five ports, including Shanghai, on equal terms with the British. The Qing court, mindful of the great losses suffered in the Opium War, readily agreed. On May 18th, Daoguang 24th year, they ordered Liangguang Governor-General Qiying to sign the Sino-American Treaty of Commerce with American envoy Caleb Cushing. Then, on September 13th of the same year, they ordered Imperial Commissioner Qiying to sign the Sino-French Treaty of Amity with French Plenipotentiary Minister Théodose de Lagrené. From then on, Shanghai became a commercial battleground divided by international imperialism. (To be continued)

Please Take Home a Bit of Artistic Impression 196

The League of Actors' Grand Performance. As a rule, all members currently in Shanghai must perform on stage. However, the time for the performances is limited, and each play can only accommodate a limited number of main characters. Moreover, the league's members often number close to a thousand. Trying to have a thousand actors perform in six or seven hours across a dozen or so plays creates a great difficulty in allocation, as there are too many monks and not enough gruel. Therefore, the solution of having eight or ten people jointly play one role was devised. Although this method is lively and pleasing, each actor's time on stage is too short, making it impossible to fully showcase their strengths, which is somewhat unsatisfactory. Furthermore, there are many plays that cannot be divided into scenes, so a large number of actors are asked to appear on stage at the same time. For example, in "Heavenly Maidens Scattering Flowers," eight heavenly maidens appear on stage together to sing; in "Hanjinkou," seven or eight Guan Gongs run out. Ultimately, this does not align with the logic of the story, and the audience is left bewildered, unable to discern who is superior. Therefore, starting from the last league performance, the method was changed. Instead of trying to include everyone, it's better to eliminate the crude and retain the refined, and specifically invite a few outstanding performers who have never had the opportunity to share the stage before to unite. Each role is played by one actor from beginning to end, with particular emphasis on the careful selection of the script. Only in this way can the artistry of the actors be fully expressed, and the audience can have a truly good show to watch. Because the purpose of the League of Actors' grand performance is not only to raise funds but also to promote the art of the acting world. It's definitely not just about getting everyone to spend money to watch a lively but ultimately empty show. At the very least, it should leave the audience with a bit of artistic impression, making them feel that these good plays are simply unavailable anywhere else except at the League of Actors' grand performance.

This year's League of Actors' grand performance is being done in this spirit. If you encounter such a grand event again, it will be at least a year later, because the League of Actors only actively organizes a grand performance once a year unless there are special circumstances. For acting events organized by outside parties, we will not issue a mobilization order for all members.

For the reasons mentioned above, we only have two plays in this year's grand performance. One is the complete "Crying at the Ancestral Temple," and the other is the complete "Tale of the Pipa."

Famous People and Famous Plays Shine Together 197

"Crying at the Ancestral Temple" is an extremely difficult play to sing. Since the death of Wang Lingyin, although others have performed it, few have been able to achieve acclaim. This is because the protagonist, Prince Beilou Liu Chen, struggles fiercely with Liu Adou in the first scene, arguing that "surrendering to the enemy is worse than dying in battle," and then in the second scene, he meets Lady Cui and sacrifices his family for the country. The plot is extremely tense, making the performance very demanding. Immediately afterward, he has to perform "Crying at the Ancestral Temple," with very little time for rest in between. The large sections of singing in "Crying at the Ancestral Temple" are divided into seven parts, with over a hundred lines in total, making it even more strenuous than singing "Bumping into the Monument." If the skill is even slightly lacking, it is difficult to avoid becoming hoarse and exhausted. Therefore, those who study Wang Lingyin's style of old male roles all regard this play with trepidation.

Madam Du is a famous socialite in Shanghai with a unique talent and profound knowledge. Not to mention that ordinary amateur actors cannot hope to match her, even renowned veterans of the acting world often sigh in admiration. Madam Du has put in a lot of deep study of the play "Crying at the Ancestral Temple." Therefore, she is able to handle it with ease. The League of Actors' performance has reached its 22nd iteration, and it has never previously relied on any outside performers. However, this time, they specifically and earnestly invited Madam Du to join and help. This is clear proof that Madam Du's art is able to convince all members of the League.

Madam Du is usually unwilling to easily appear in public. This time, it is truly because the matter concerns public welfare that she condescended to accept after the League repeatedly requested her. Not only is the League extremely grateful, but the audience will also be blessed with a rare treat. To add icing on the cake, the League has specially selected renowned actors to fill the supporting roles, aiming to make this performance of "Crying at the Ancestral Temple" the best in China's history.

The important role directly opposite Madam Du is Lady Cui, specially played by Ms. Li Huijin, a Kunqu actress skilled in tragic roles. They have rehearsed the scene of sacrificing the family countless times and have become extremely well-coordinated. It is expected that this scene will surely draw many tears. Please bring an extra handkerchief to the performance.

Deng Ai, China's first stuttering general, is an ambitious and ruthless warlord whose position is extremely important, and he will be performed by Mr. Zhou Xinfang. Zhuge Zhan and his son, in the face of extreme national crisis, disregarded the dangers and led the Shu troops, vowing to resist the enemy to the death. This spirit of saving the country can serve as a model for future generations of soldiers, and they will be played by Mr. Lin Shusen and Mr. Gao Xueqiao, respectively. One is loyal and devoted, and the other is courageous and fierce. Watching them can inspire the corrupt and cowardly.

Other roles, such as Chen Hefeng's Zhang Yi, Dong Zhiyang's Deng Zhong, Liu Kunrong's Ma Miao, Han Jinkui's Huang Hao, Zhao Dongsheng's Zhong Hui, Chen Jialin's Liu Shan, and Liu Wenmei's Lady Li, are all carefully selected from each troupe and are suited to each person's personality. They will all be able to perform in a fitting manner.

A Perfect Match in the Tale of the Pipa 198

To harmonize the audience's emotions, the League has, in addition to the national affairs play "Crying at the Ancestral Temple," also arranged a good social play, [the complete Tale of the Pipa]. The name of this play is so fragrant and elegant, and one can tell at a glance that it is a good play of joy and sorrow, separation and reunion, that can deeply move people. Mr. Xiao Yang Yuelou plays the female lead, Qin Xianglian, a deserted woman with a tragic fate, and his performance is extremely mournful and beautiful, making people heartbroken. Mr. Zhao Ruquan plays the male lead, Wang Yanling, a gentleman who speaks out for justice, combining solemnity and humor, which is hilarious. In addition, there is another important role, Chen Shimei, played by Mr. Zhang Guifen. He plays a heartless man, with both singing and acting emphasized, and there are many wonderful parts. Combining the best actors from the three theaters on one stage to play the main characters in the play truly makes for a genuine and high-quality "perfect match" play.
